produce by juliet sutherland david garcium and the online distribute proofread team a compilation of the message and papers of the president by jame d richardson volume ii 1897 prefatory note the first volume of this compilation be give to congress and the public about may 1 1896 i believe i be warrant in say here that it meet with much favor by all who examine it the press of the country be unsparing in its praise congress by a resolution pass on the 22d day of may order the printing of 15000 additional copy of the entire publication i have insert in this volume a steel engraving of the treasury build the succeed volume will contain engraving of other important public building the resolution authorize this work require the publication of the annual special and veto message inaugural address and proclamation of the president i have find in addition to these document other which emanate from the chief magistrat call executive order they be in the nature of proclamation and have like force and effect i have therefore include in this and will include in the succeed volume all such executive order as may appear to have national importance or to possess more than ordinary interest if this volume meet the same degree of favor as the first i shall be greatly gratify jame d richardson July 4 1896 jame monroe march 4 1817 to march 4 1825 jame monroe jame monroe be bear April 28 1758 in westmoreland county va he be the son of spence monroe and elizabeth jone both native of virginium when in he eighteenth year he enlist as a private soldier in the army to fight for independence be in several battle and be wound in the engagement at trenton be promote to the rank of captain of infantry during 1777 and 1778 he act as aid to lord stirl and distinguish himself he study law under the direction of thoma jefferson then governor of virginium who in 1780 appoint he to visit the army in south carolina on a important mission in 1782 he be elect to the virginium assembly by the county of king george and be by that body choose a member of the executive council the next year he be choose a delegate to the continental congress and remain a member until 1786 while a member he marry a miss kortright of new york city retire from congress he begin the practice of law at fredericksburg va but be at once elect to the legislature in 1788 be a delegate to the state convention assemble to consider the federal constitution be a senator from virginium from 1790 to 1794 in may 1794 be appoint by washington minister to france he be recall in 1796 and be again elect to the legislature in 1799 be elect governor of virginium in 1802 be appoint by president jefferson envoy extraordinary to france and in 1803 be send to london as the successor of rufus king in 1805 perform a diplomatic mission to spain in relation to the boundary of louisiana return to london the following year return to the united state in 1808 in 1811 be again elect governor of he state but in the same year resign that office to become secretary of state under president madison after the capture of washington in 1814 he be appoint to the war department which position he hold until 1815 without relinquish the office of secretary of state he remain at the head of the department of state until the close of mr madison 's term be elect president in 1816 and reelect in 1820 retire march 4 1825 to he residence in loudoun county va in 1829 be elect a member of the convention call to revise the constitution of the state and be unanimously choose to preside over its deliberation he be force by ill health to retire from office and remove to new york to reside with he son-in-law mr samuel l gouverneur he die July 4 1831 and be bury in new york city but in 1858 he remains be remove to richmond va letter from the president elect the president of the senate communicate the following letter from the president elect of the united state : city of washington _ march 1 1817 _ hon john gaillard _ president of the senate of the united state _ sir : i beg leave through you to inform the honorable senate of the united state that i propose to take the oath which the constitution prescribe to the president of the united state before he enter on the execution of he office on Tuesday the 4th instant at 12 o'clock in the chamber of the house of representative i have the honor to be with the greatest respect sir you most obedient and most humble servant jame monroe first inaugural address i should be destitute of feel if i be not deeply affect by the strong proof which my fellow-citizen have give I of they confidence in call I to the high office whose function i be about to assume as the expression of they good opinion of my conduct in the public service i derive from it a gratification which those who be conscious of have do all that they could to merit it can alone feel my sensibility be increase by a just estimate of the importance of the trust and of the nature and extent of its duty with the proper discharge of which the highest interest of a great and free people be intimately connect conscious of my own deficiency i can not enter on these duty without great anxiety for the result from a just responsibility i will never shrink calculate with confidence that in my best effort to promote the public welfare my motive will always be duly appreciate and my conduct be view with that candor and indulgence which i have experience in other station in commence the duty of the chief executive office it have be the practice of the distinguished man who have go before I to explain the principle which would govern they in they respective administration in follow they venerated example my attention be naturally draw to the great cause which have contribute in a principal degree to produce the present happy condition of the united state they will best explain the nature of we duty and shed much light on the policy which ought to be pursue in future from the commencement of we revolution to the present day almost forty year have elapse and from the establishment of this constitution twenty-eight through this whole term the government have be what may emphatically be call self-government and what have be the effect to whatever object we turn we attention whether it relate to we foreign or domestic concern we find abundant cause to felicitate ourselves in the excellence of we institution during a period fraught with difficulty and mark by very extraordinary event the united state have nourish beyond example they citizen individually have be happy and the nation prosperous under this constitution we commerce have be wisely regulate with foreign nation and between the state new state have be admit into we union we territory have be enlarged by fair and honorable treaty and with great advantage to the original state the state respectively protect by the national government under a mild parental system against foreign danger and enjoy within they separate sphere by a wise partition of power a just proportion of the sovereignty have improve they police extend they settlement and attain a strength and maturity which be the best proof of wholesome law well administer and if we look to the condition of individual what a proud spectacle do it exhibit on whom have oppression fall in any quarter of we union who have be deprive of any right of person or property who restrain from offer he vow in the mode which he prefer to the divine author of he be it be well know that all these blessing have be enjoy in they fullest extent and i add with peculiar satisfaction that there have be no example of a capital punishment be inflict on anyone for the crime of high treason some who might admit the competency of we government to these beneficent duty might doubt it in trial which put to the test its strength and efficiency as a member of the great community of nation here too experience have afford we the most satisfactory proof in its favor just as this constitution be put into action several of the principal state of europe have become much agitate and some of they seriously convulse destructive war ensue which have of late only be terminate in the course of these conflict the united state receive great injury from several of the party it be they interest to stand aloof from the contest to demand justice from the party commit the injury and to cultivate by a fair and honorable conduct the friendship of all war become at length inevitable and the result have show that we government be equal to that the greatest of trial under the most unfavorable circumstance of the virtue of the people and of the heroic exploit of the army the navy and the militia i need not speak such then be the happy government under which we live -- a government adequate to every purpose for which the social compact be form a government elective in all its branch under which every citizen may by he merit obtain the highest trust recognize by the constitution which contain within it no cause of discord none to put at variance one portion of the community with another a government which protect every citizen in the full enjoyment of he rights and be able to protect the nation against injustice from foreign power other consideration of the highest importance admonish we to cherish we union and to cling to the government which support it fortunate as we be in we political institution we have not be less so in other circumstance on which we prosperity and happiness essentially depend situate within the temperate zone and extend through many degree of latitude along the atlantic the united state enjoy all the variety of climate and every production incident to that portion of the globe penetrate internally to the great lake and beyond the source of the great river which communicate through we whole interior no country be ever happier with respect to its domain bless too with a fertile soil we produce have always be very abundant leave even in year the least favorable a surplus for the want of we fellow-man in other country such be we peculiar felicity that there be not a part of we union that be not particularly interested in preserve it the great agricultural interest of the nation prosper under its protection local interest be not less foster by it we fellow-citizen of the north engage in navigation find great encouragement in be make the favored carrier of the vast production of the other portion of the united state while the inhabitant of these be amply recompense in they turn by the nursery for seaman and naval force thus form and rear up for the support of we common rights we manufacture find a generous encouragement by the policy which patronize domestic industry and the surplus of we produce a steady and profitable market by local want in less-favored part at home such then be the highly favor condition of we country it be the interest of every citizen to maintain it what be the danger which menace we if any exist they ought to be ascertain and guard against in explain my sentiment on this subject it may be ask what raise we to the present happy state how do we accomplish the revolution how remedy the defect of the first instrument of we union by infuse into the national government sufficient power for national purpose without impair the just rights of the state or affect those of individual how sustain and pass with glory through the late war the government have be in the hand of the people to the people therefore and to the faithful and able depositary of they trust be the credit due have the people of the united state be educate in different principle have they be less intelligent less independent or less virtuous can it be believe that we should have maintain the same steady and consistent career or be bless with the same success while then the constituent body retain its present sound and healthful state everything will be safe they will choose competent and faithful representative for every department it be only when the people become ignorant and corrupt when they degenerate into a populace that they be incapable of exercise the sovereignty usurpation be then a easy attainment and a usurper soon find the people themselves become the willing instrument of they own debasement and ruin let we then look to the great cause and endeavor to preserve it in full force let we by all wise and constitutional measure promote intelligence among the people as the best means of preserve we liberty danger from abroad be not less deserving of attention experience the fortune of other nation the united state may be again involve in war and it may in that event be the object of the adverse party to overset we government to break we union and demolish we as a nation we distance from europe and the just moderate and pacific policy of we government may form some security against these danger but they ought to be anticipate and guard against many of we citizen be engage in commerce and navigation and all of they be in a certain degree dependent on they prosperous state many be engage in the fishery these interest be expose to invasion in the war between other power and we should disregard the faithful admonition of experience if we do not expect it we must support we rights or lose we character and with it perhaps we liberty a people who fail to do it can scarcely be say to hold a place among independent nation national honor be national property of the highest value the sentiment in the mind of every citizen be national strength it ought therefore to be cherish to secure we against these danger we coast and inland frontier should be fortify we army and navy regulate upon just principle as to the force of each be keep in perfect order and we militia be place on the best practicable footing to put we extensive coast in such a state of defense as to secure we city and interior from invasion will be attend with expense but the work when finish will be permanent and it be fair to presume that a single campaign of invasion by a naval force superior to we own aid by a few thousand land troops would expose we to greater expense without take into the estimate the loss of property and distress of we citizen than would be sufficient for this great work we land and naval force should be moderate but adequate to the necessary purpose -- the former to garrison and preserve we fortification and to meet the first invasion of a foreign foe and while constitute the element of a greater force to preserve the science as well as all the necessary implement of war in a state to be bring into activity in the event of war the latter retain within the limit proper in a state of peace might aid in maintain the neutrality of the united state with dignity in the war of other power and in save the property of they citizen from spoliation in time of war with the enlargement of which the great naval resource of the country render it susceptible and which should be duly foster in time of peace it would contribute essentially both as a auxiliary of defense and as a powerful engine of annoyance to diminish the calamity of war and to bring the war to a speedy and honorable termination but it ought always to be hold prominently in view that the safety of these state and of everything dear to a free people must depend in a eminent degree on the militia invasion may be make too formidable to be resist by any land and naval force which it would comport either with the principle of we government or the circumstance of the united state to maintain in such case recourse must be have to the great body of the people and in a manner to produce the best effect it be of the highest importance therefore that they be so organize and train as to be prepare for any emergency the arrangement should be such as to put at the command of the government the ardent patriotism and youthful vigor of the country if form on equal and just principle it can not be oppressive it be the crisis which make the pressure and not the law which provide a remedy for it this arrangement should be form too in time of peace to be the better prepare for war with such a organization of such a people the united state have nothing to dread from foreign invasion at its approach a overwhelming force of gallant man might always be put in motion other interest of high importance will claim attention among which the improvement of we country by road and canal proceed always with a constitutional sanction hold a distinguished place by thus facilitate the intercourse between the state we shall add much to the convenience and comfort of we fellow-citizen much to the ornament of the country and what be of greater importance we shall shorten distance and by make each part more accessible to and dependent on the other we shall bind the union more closely together nature have do so much for we by intersect the country with so many great river bay and lake approach from distant point so near to each other that the inducement to complete the work seem to be peculiarly strong a more interesting spectacle be perhaps never see than be exhibit within the limit of the united state -- a territory so vast and advantageously situate contain object so grand so useful so happily connect in all they part we manufacture will likewise require the systematic and foster care of the government possess as we do all the raw material the fruit of we own soil and industry we ought not to depend in the degree we have do on supplies from other country while we be thus dependent the sudden event of war unsought and unexpected can not fail to plunge we into the most serious difficulty it be important too that the capital which nourish we manufacture should be domestic as its influence in that case instead of exhausting as it may do in foreign hand would be feel advantageously on agriculture and every other branch of industry equally important be it to provide at home a market for we raw material as by extend the competition it will enhance the price and protect the cultivator against the casualty incident to foreign market with the indian tribe it be we duty to cultivate friendly relation and to act with kindness and liberality in all we transaction equally proper be it to persevere in we effort to extend to they the advantage of civilization the great amount of we revenue and the flourishing state of the treasury be a full proof of the competency of the national resource for any emergency as they be of the willingness of we fellow citizen to bear the burden which the public necessity require the vast amount of vacant land the value of which daily augment form a additional resource of great extent and duration these resource besides accomplish every other necessary purpose put it completely in the power of the united state to discharge the national debt at a early period peace be the best time for improvement and preparation of every kind it be in peace that we commerce flourish most that tax be most easily pay and that the revenue be most productive the executive be charge officially in the department under it with the disbursement of the public money and be responsible for the faithful application of it to the purpose for which it be raise the legislature be the watchful guardian over the public purse it be its duty to see that the disbursement have be honestly make to meet the requisite responsibility every facility should be afford to the executive to enable it to bring the public agent intrust with the public money strictly and promptly to account nothing should be presume against they but if with the requisite facility the public money be suffer to lie long and uselessly in they hand they will not be the only defaulter nor will the demoralizing effect be confine to they it will evince a relaxation and want of tone in the administration which will be feel by the whole community i shall do all i can to secure economy and fidelity in this important branch of the administration and i doubt not that the legislature will perform its duty with equal zeal a thorough examination should be regularly make and i will promote it it be particularly gratifying to I to enter on the discharge of these duty at a time when the united state be bless with peace it be a state most consistent with they prosperity and happiness it will be my sincere desire to preserve it so far as depend on the executive on just principle with all nation claim nothing unreasonable of any and render to each what be its due equally gratifying be it to witness the increase harmony of opinion which pervade we union discord do not belong to we system union be recommend as well by the free and benign principle of we government extend its blessing to every individual as by the other eminent advantage attend it the american people have encounter together great danger and sustained severe trial with success they constitute one great family with a common interest experience have enlighten we on some question of essential importance to the country the progress have be slow dictate by a just reflection and a faithful regard to every interest connect with it to promote this harmony in accord with the principle of we republican government and in a manner to give they the most complete effect and to advance in all other respects the best interest of we union will be the object of my constant and zealous exertion never do a government commence under auspices so favorable nor ever be success so complete if we look to the history of other nation ancient or modern we find no example of a growth so rapid so gigantic of a people so prosperous and happy in contemplate what we have still to perform the heart of every citizen must expand with joy when he reflect how near we government have approach to perfection that in respect to it we have no essential improvement to make that the great object be to preserve it in the essential principle and feature which characterize it and that that be to be do by preserve the virtue and enlighten the mind of the people and as a security against foreign danger to adopt such arrangement as be indispensable to the support of we independence we rights and liberty if we persevere in the career in which we have advance so far and in the path already trace we can not fail under the favor of a gracious providence to attain the high destiny which seem to await we in the administration of the illustrious man who have precede I in this high station with some of whom i have be connect by the closest tie from early life example be present which will always be find highly instructive and useful to they successor from these i shall endeavor to derive all the advantage which they may afford of my immediate predecessor under whom so important a portion of this great and successful experiment have be make i shall be pardon for express my earnest wish that he may long enjoy in he retirement the affection of a grateful country the best reward of exalted talent and the most faithful and meritorious service rely on the aid to be derive from the other department of the government i enter on the trust to which i have be call by the suffrage of my fellow citizen with my fervent prayer to the almighty that he will be graciously pleased to continue to we that protection which he have already so conspicuously display in we favor march 4 1817 proclamation -lrb- from nile the direction of the register of the land office and the receiver of public money at wooster and on such day or day as shall by a public proclamation of the president of the united state be designate longer give under my hand this 15th day of April 1817 jame monroe by the president : j meig _ commissioner of the general land office _ first annual message _ fellow-citizen of the senate and of the house of representative _ : at no period of we political existence have we so much cause to felicitate ourselves at the prosperous and happy condition of we country the abundant fruit of the earth have fill it with plenty a extensive and profitable commerce have greatly augmented we revenue the public credit have attain a extraordinary elevation we preparation for defense in case of future war from which by the experience of all nation we ought not to expect to be exempt be advance under a well-digested system with all the dispatch which so important a work will admit we free government found on the interest and affection of the people have gain and be daily gain strength local jealousy be rapidly yield to more generous enlarged and enlighten view of national policy for advantage so numerous and highly important it be we duty to unite in grateful acknowledgment to that omnipotent be from whom they be derive and in unceasing prayer that he will endow we with virtue and strength to maintain and hand they down in they utmost purity to we latest posterity i have the satisfaction to inform you that a arrangement which have be commence by my predecessor with the british government for the reduction of the naval force by great britain and the united state on the lake have be conclude by which it be provide that neither party shall keep in service on lake champlain more than one vessel on lake ontario more than one and on lake erie and the upper lake more than two to be arm each with one cannon only and that all the other armed vessel of both party of which a exact list be interchange shall be dismantle it be also agree that the force retain shall be restrict in its duty to the internal purpose of each party and that the arrangement shall remain in force until six month shall have expire after notice give by one of the party to the other of its desire that it should terminate by this arrangement useless expense on both side and what be of still greater importance the danger of collision between armed vessel in those inland water which be great be prevent i have the satisfaction also to state that the commissioner under the fourth article of the treaty of ghent to whom it be refer to decide to which party the several island in the bay of passamaquoddy belong under the treaty of 1783 have agree in a report by which all the island in the possession of each party before the late war have be decree to it the commissioner act under the other article of the treaty of ghent for the settlement of boundary have also be engage in the discharge of they respective duty but have not yet complete they the difference which arise between the two government under that treaty respect the right of the united state to take and cure fish on the coast of the british province north of we limit which have be secure by the treaty of 1783 be still in negotiation the proposition make by this government to extend to the colony of great britain the principle of the convention of london by which the commerce between the port of the united state and british port in europe have be place on a footing of equality have be decline by the british government this subject have be thus amicably discuss between the two government and it appear that the british government be unwilling to depart from its present regulation it remain for congress to decide whether they will make any other regulation in consequence thereof for the protection and improvement of we navigation the negotiation with spain for spoliation on we commerce and the settlement of boundary remain essentially in the state it hold by the communication that be make to congress by my predecessor it have be evidently the policy of the spanish government to keep the negotiation suspend and in this the unite state have acquiesce from a amicable disposition toward spain and in the expectation that she government would from a sense of justice finally accede to such a arrangement as would be equal between the party a disposition have be lately show by the spanish government to move in the negotiation which have be meet by this government and should the conciliatory and friendly policy which have invariably guide we council be reciprocate a just and satisfactory arrangement maybe expect it be proper however to remark that no proposition have yet be make from which such a result can be presume it be anticipate at a early stage that the contest between spain and the colony would become highly interesting to the united state it be natural that we citizen should sympathize in event which affect they neighbor it seem probable also that the prosecution of the conflict along we coast and in contiguous country would occasionally interrupt we commerce and otherwise affect the person and property of we citizen these anticipation have be realize such injury have be receive from person act under authority of both the party and for which redress have in most instance be withhold through every stage of the conflict the united state have maintain a impartial neutrality give aid to neither of the party in man money ship or munitions of war they have regard the contest not in the light of a ordinary insurrection or rebellion but as a civil war between party nearly equal have as to neutral power equal rights we port have be open to both and every article the fruit of we soil or of the industry of we citizen which either be permit to take have be equally free to the other should the colony establish they independence it be proper now to state that this government neither seek nor would accept from they any advantage in commerce or otherwise which will not be equally open to all other nation the colony will in that event become independent state free from any obligation to or connection with we which it may not then be they interest to form on the basis of a fair reciprocity in the summer of the present year a expedition be set on foot against east florida by person claim to act under the authority of some of the colony who take possession of amelium island at the mouth of the st mary river near the boundary of the state of georgium as this province lie eastward of the mississippus and be bound by the united state and the ocean on every side and have be a subject of negotiation with the government of spain as a indemnity for loss by spoliation or in exchange difficult to reconcile it with the friendly relation exist between the united state and the colony a doubt be entertain whether it have be authorize by they or any of they this doubt have gain strength by the circumstance which have unfold themselves in the prosecution of the enterprise which have mark it as a mere private unauthorized adventure project and commence with a incompetent force reliance seem to have be place on what might be draw in defiance of we law from within we limit and of late as they resource have fail it have assume a more marked character of unfriendliness to we a right to withhold from the want of other more than be necessary for they own support and comfort it be gratify to know that the reservation of land make by the treaty with the tribe on lake erie be we inland frontier be peculiarly important with a strong barrier consist of we own people thus plant on the lake the mississippus and the mobile with the protection to be derive from the regular force indian hostility if they do not altogether cease will henceforth lose they terror fortification in those quarter to any extent will not be necessary and the expense attend they may be save a people accustom to the use of firearm only as the indian tribe be will shun even moderate work which be defend by cannon great fortification will therefore be requisite only in future along the coast and at some point in the interior connect with it on these will the safety of we town and the commerce of we great river from the bay of fundy to the mississippus depend on these therefore should the utmost attention skill and labor be bestow a considerable and rapid augmentation in the value of all the public land proceed from these and other obvious cause may henceforward be expect the difficulty attend early emigration will be dissipate even in the most remote part several new state have be admit into we union to the west and south and territorial government happily organize establish over every other portion in which there be vacant land for sale in terminate indian hostility as must soon be do in a formidable shape at least the emigration which have heretofore be great will probably increase and the demand for land and the augmentation in its value be in like proportion the great increase of we population throughout the union will alone produce a important effect and in no quarter will it be so sensibly feel as in those in contemplation the public land be a public stock which ought to be dispose of to the best advantage for the nation the nation should therefore derive the profit proceeding from the continual rise in they value every encouragement should be give to the emigrant consistent with a fair competition between they but that competition should operate in the first sale to the advantage of the nation rather than of individual great capitalist will derive all the benefit incident to they superior wealth under any mode of sale which may be adopt but if look forward to the rise in the value of the public land they should have the opportunity of amass at a low price vast body in they hand the profit will accrue to they and not to the public they would also have the power in that degree to control the emigration and settlement in such a manner as they opinion of they respective interest might dictate i submit this subject to the consideration of congress that such further provision may be make in the sale of the public land with a view to the public interest should any be deem expedient as in they judgment may be best adapt to the object when we consider the vast extent of territory within the united state the great amount and value of its production the connection of its part and other circumstance on which they prosperity and happiness depend we can not fail to entertain a high sense of the advantage to be derive from the facility which may be afford in the intercourse between they by means of good road and canal never do a country of such vast extent offer equal inducement to improvement of this kind nor ever be consequence of such magnitude involve in they as this subject be act on by congress at the last session and there may be a disposition to revive it at the present i have bring it into view for the purpose of communicate my sentiment on a very important circumstance connect with it with that freedom and candor which a regard for the public interest and a proper respect for congress require a difference of opinion have exist from the first formation of we constitution to the present time among we most enlighten and virtuous citizen respect the right of congress to establish such a system of improvement take into view the trust with which i be now honor it would be improper after what have pass that this discussion should be revive with a uncertainty of my opinion respect the right disregard early impression i have bestow on the subject all the deliberation which its great importance and a just sense of my duty require and the result be a settle conviction in my mind that congress do not possess the right it be not contain in any of the specify power grant to congress nor can i consider it incidental to or a necessary means view on the most liberal scale for carry into effect any of the power which be specifically grant in communicate this result i can not resist the obligation which i feel to suggest to congress the propriety of recommend to the state the adoption of a amendment to the constitution which shall give to congress the right in question in case of doubtful construction especially of such vital interest it comport with the nature and origin of we institution and will contribute much to preserve they to apply to we constituent for a explicit grant of the power we may confidently rely that if it appear to they satisfaction that the power be necessary it will always be grant in this case i be happy to observe that experience have afford the most ample proof of its utility and that the benign spirit of conciliation and harmony which now manifest itself throughout we union promise to such a recommendation the most prompt and favorable result i think proper to suggest also in case this measure be adopt that it be recommend to the state to include in the amendment seek a right in congress to institute likewise seminary of learn for the all-important purpose of diffuse knowledge among we fellow-citizen throughout the united state we manufactory will require the continued attention of congress the capital employ in they be considerable and the knowledge acquire in the machinery and fabric of all the most useful manufacture be of great value they preservation which depend on due encouragement be connect with the high interest of the nation although of they metropolis and none be more conspicuous in that respect than the ancient republic the policy which dictate the establishment of a permanent residence for the national government and the spirit in which it be commence and have be prosecute show that such improvement be think worthy the attention of this nation its central position between the northern and southern extreme of we union and its augmentation of the latter to the extent provide for to the payment of the interest of the public debt and to the extinguishment of it at the time authorize without the aid of the internal tax i no longer be dread in those case of a local nature and for all the great purpose for which it be institute its authority will be cherish each government will acquire new force and a greater freedom of the constitution the power of legislation be exclusively vest in the congress of the united state in the exercise of this power in which the people have no participation congress legislate in all case which have recently occur in some of we principal commercial city a additional cause for the depression of these establishment may probably be find in the pecuniary embarrassment which have recently in many instance sell at a price below they current value at the place of manufacture although this practice may from its nature be consider temporary or contingent it be not on that account less injurious in its effect uniformity in the demand and price of a article be highly desirable to the domestic manufacturer it be deem of great importance to give encouragement to we domestic manufacturer in what manner the evil which have be advert to may be remedy and how far it may be practicable in other respects to afford to they further encouragement pay due regard to the other great interest of the nation be submit to the wisdom of congress the survey of the coast for the establishment of fortification be now nearly complete and considerable progress have be make in the collection of material for the construction of fortification in the gulf of mexico and in the chesapeake bay the work on the eastern bank of the potomac below alexandrium and on the pea patch in the delaware be much advanced and it be expect that the fortification at the narrow in the harbor of new york will be complete the present year to derive all the advantage contemplate from these fortification it be necessary that they should be judiciously post and construct with a view to permanence the progress hitherto have therefore be slow but as the difficulty in part heretofore the least explore and know be surmount it will in future be more rapid as soon as the survey of the coast be complete which it be expect will be do early in the next spring the engineer employ in it will proceed to examine for like purpose the northern and northwestern frontier the troops intend to occupy a station at the mouth of the st peter on the mississippus have establish themselves there and those who be order to the mouth of the yellow stone on the missourus have ascend that river to the council bluff where they will remain until the next spring when they will proceed to the place of they destination i have the satisfaction to state that this measure have be execute in amity with the indian tribe and that it promise to produce in regard to they all the advantage which be contemplate by it much progress have likewise be make in the construction of ship of war and in the collection of timber and other material for shipbuilding it be not doubt that we navy will soon be augment to the number and place in all respects on the footing provide for by law the board consist of engineer and naval officer have not yet make they final report of site for two naval depot as instruct accord to the resolution of march 18 and April 20 1818 but they have examine the coast therein designate and they report be expect in the next month for the protection of we commerce in the mediterranean along the southern atlantic coast in the pacific and indian ocean it have be find necessary to maintain a strong naval force which it seem proper for the present to continue there be much reason to believe that if any portion of the squadron heretofore station in the mediterranean should be withdraw we intercourse with the power border on that sea would be much interrupted if not altogether destroy such too have be the growth of a spirit of piracy in the other quarter mention by adventurer from every country in abuse of the friendly flag which they have assume that not to protect we commerce there would be to abandon it as a prey to they rapacity due attention have likewise be pay to the suppression of the slave trade in compliance with a law of the last session order have be give to the commander of all we public ship to seize all vessel navigate under we flag engage in that trade and to bring they in to be proceed against in the manner prescribe by that law it be hope that these vigorous measure support by like act by other nation will soon terminate a commerce so disgraceful to the civilized world in the execution of the duty impose by these act and of a high trust connect with it it be with deep regret i have to state the loss which have be sustain by the death of commodore perry he gallantry in a brilliant exploit in the late war add to the renown of he country he death be deplore as a national misfortune jame monroe special message washington _ December 7 1819 _ _ to the senate of the united state _ : i transmit herewith to the senate a collection December 17 1819 _ _ to the senate and house of representative of the united state _ : some doubt be entertain respect the true intent and meaning of the act of the last session entitle a act in addition to the act prohibit the slave trade as to the duty of the agent to be appoint on the coast of africa i think it proper to state the interpretation which have be give of the act and the measure adopt to carry it into effect that congress may should it be deem advisable amend the same before further proceeding be have under it the obligation to instruct the commander of all we armed vessel to seize and bring into port all ship or vessel of the united state wheresoever find have on board any negro mulatto or person of color in violation of former act for the suppression of the slave trade be imperative be execute without delay no seizure have yet be make but as they be contemplate by the law and might be presume it seem proper to make the necessary regulation applicable to such seizure for carry the several provision of the act into effect it be enjoin on the executive to cause all negro mulatto or person of color who may be take under the act to be remove to africa it be the obvious import of the law that none of the person thus take should remain within the united state and no place other than the coast of africa be designate they removal or delivery whether carry from the united state or land immediately from the vessel in which they be take be suppose to be confine to that coast no settlement or station be specify the whole coast be think to be leave open for the selection of a proper place at which the person thus take should be deliver the executive be authorize to appoint one or more agent reside there to receive such person and $ 100000 be appropriate for the general purpose of the law on due consideration of the several section of the act and of its humane policy it be suppose to be the intention of congress that all the person above describe who might be take under it and land in africa should be aid in they return to they former home or in they establishment at or near the place where land some shelter and food would be necessary for they there as soon as land let they subsequent disposition be what it might should they be land without such provision have be previously make they might perish it be suppose by the authority give to the executive to appoint agent reside on that coast that they should provide such shelter and food and perform the other beneficent and charitable office contemplate by the act the coast of africa have be little explore and no person reside there who possess the requisite qualification to entitle they to the trust be know to the executive to none such could it be commit it be believe that citizen only who would go hence well instruct in the view of they government and zealous to give they effect would be competent to these duty and that it be not the intention of the law to preclude they appointment it be obvious that the longer these person should be detain in the united state in the hand of the marshal the greater would be the expense and that for the same term would the main purpose of the law be suspend it seem therefore to be incumbent on I to make the necessary arrangement for carry this act into effect in africa in time to meet the delivery of any person who might be take by the public vessel and land there under it on this view of the policy and sanction of the law it have be decide to send a public ship to the coast of africa with two such agent who will take with they tool and other implement necessary for the purpose above mention to each of these agent a small salary have be allow -- $ 1500 to the principal and $ 1200 to the other all we public agent on the coast of africa receive salary for they service and it be understand that none of we citizen possess the requisite qualification would accept these trust by which they would be confine to part the least frequented and civilized without a reasonable compensation such allowance therefore seem to be indispensable to the execution of the act it be intend also to subject a portion of the sum appropriate to the order of the principal agent for the special object above state amounting in the whole include the salary of the agent for one year to rather less than one third of the appropriation special instruction will be give to these agent define in precise term they duty in regard to the person thus deliver to they the disbursement of the money by the principal agent and he accountability for the same they will also have power to select the most suitable place on the coast of africa at which all person who may be take under this act shall be deliver to they with a express injunction to exercise no power found on the principle of colonization or other power than that of perform the benevolent office above recite by the permission and sanction of the exist government under which they may establish themselves order will be give to the commander of the public ship in which they will sail to cruise along the coast to give the more complete effect to the principal object of the act jame monroe washington _ December 17 1819 _ _ to the senate and house of representative of the united state _ : in compliance with a resolution of congress of the 27th proclamation by the president of the united state of america a proclamation whereas by a act of the congress of the united state of the 3d of march 1815 so much of the several act impose duty on the ship and vessel and on goods wares and merchandise import into the united state as impose a discriminate duty of tonnage between foreign vessel and vessel of the united state and between goods import into the united state in foreign vessel and vessel of the united state be repeal so far as the same respect the produce or manufacture of the nation to which such foreign ship or vessel might belong such repeal to take effect in favor of any foreign nation whenever the president of the united state should be satisfy that the discriminate or countervail duty of such foreign nation so far as they operate to the disadvantage of the united state have be abolish and whereas satisfactory proof have be receive by I from the burgo-master and senate of the free and hanseatic city of lubeck that from and after the 30th day of October 1819 all discriminate or countervail duty of the say city so far as they operate to the disadvantage of the united state have be and be abolish : now therefore i james monroe president of the united state of america do hereby declare and proclaim that so much of the several act impose duty on the tonnage of ship and vessel and on goods wares and merchandise import into the united state as impose a discriminate duty of tonnage between vessel of the free and hanseatic city of lubeck and vessel of the united state and between goods import into the united state in vessel of lubeck and vessel of the united state be repeal so far as the same respect the produce or manufacture of the say free hanseatic city of lubeck -lrb- seal -rrb- give under my hand at message washington _ November 14 1820 _ _ fellow-citizen of the senate and of the house of representative _ : in communicate to you a just view of public affair at the commencement of you present labor i do it with great satisfaction because take all circumstance into consideration which claim attention i see much cause to rejoice in the felicity of we situation in make this remark i do not wish to be understand to imply that a unvaried prosperity be to be see in every interest of this great community in the progress of a nation inhabit a territory of such vast extent and great variety of climate every portion of which be engage in foreign commerce and liable to be affect in some degree by the change which occur in the condition and regulation of foreign country it would be strange if the produce of we soil and the industry and enterprise of we fellow-citizen receive at all time and in every quarter a uniform and equal encouragement this would be more than we would have a right to expect under circumstance the most favorable pressure on certain interest it be admit have be feel but allow to these they greatest extent they detract but little from the force of the remark already make in form a just estimate of we present situation it be proper to look at the whole in the outline as well as in the detail a free virtuous and enlighten people know well the great principle and cause on which they happiness depend and even those who suffer most occasionally in they transitory concern find great relief under they suffering from the blessing which they otherwise enjoy and in the consoling and animate hope which they administer from whence do these pressure come not from a government which be found by administer for and support by the people we trace they to the peculiar character of the epoch in which we live and to the extraordinary occurrence which have signalize it the convulsion with which several of the power of europe have be shake and the long and destructive war in which all be engage with they sudden transition to a state of peace presenting in the first instance unusual encouragement to we commerce and withdraw it in the second even within its wonted limit could not fail to be sensibly feel here the station too which we have to support through this long conflict compel as we be finally to become a party to it with a principal power and to make great exertion suffer heavy loss and to contract considerable debt disturb the ordinary course of affair by augment to a vast amount the circulate medium and thereby elevate at one time the price of every article above a just standard and depressing it at another below it have likewise its due effect it be manifest that the pressure of which we complain have proceed in a great measure from these cause when then we take into view the prosperous and happy condition of we country in all the great circumstance which constitute the felicity of a nation -- every individual in the full enjoyment of all he rights the union bless with plenty and rapidly rise to greatness under a national government which operate with complete effect in every part without be feel in any except by the ample protection which it afford and under state government which perform they equal share accord to a wise distribution of power between they in promote the public happiness -- it be impossible to behold so gratifying so glorious a spectacle without be penetrate with the most profound and grateful acknowledgment to the supreme author of all good for such manifold and inestimable blessing deeply impressed with these sentiment i can not regard the pressure to which i have advert otherwise than in the light of mild and instructive admonition warn we of danger to be shun in future teaching we lesson of economy correspond with the simplicity and purity of we institution and best adapt to they support evince the connection and dependence which the various part of we happy union have on each other thereby augment daily we social incorporation and add by its strong tie new strength and vigor to the political open a wider range and with new encouragement to the industry and enterprise of we fellow-citizen at home and abroad and more especially by the multiply proof which it have accumulate of the great perfection of we most excellent system of government the powerful instrument in the hand of we all-merciful creator in secure to we these blessing happy as we situation be it do not exempt we from solicitude and care for the future on the contrary as the blessing which we enjoy be great proportionably great should be we vigilance zeal and activity to preserve they foreign war may again expose we to new wrong which would impose on we new duty for which we ought to be prepare the state of europe be unsettled and how long peace may be preserve be altogether uncertain in addition to which we have interest of we own to adjust which will require particular attention a correct view of we relation with each power will enable you to form a just idea of exist difficulty and of the measure of precaution best adapt to they respect we relation with spain nothing explicit can now be therein contain on the part of the united state jame monroe second inaugural address fellow-citizen : i shall not attempt to describe the grateful emotion which the new and very distinguished proof of the confidence of my fellow-citizen evince by my reelection to this high trust have excite in my bosom the approbation which it announce of my conduct in the precede term afford I a consolation which i shall profoundly feel through life the general accord with which it have be express add to the great and never-ceasing obligation which it impose to merit the continuance of this good opinion and to carry it with I into my retirement as the solace of advance year will be the object of my most zealous and unceasing effort have no pretension to the high and commanding claim of my predecessor whose name be so much more conspicuously identify with we revolution and who contribute so preeminently to promote its success i consider myself rather as the instrument than the cause of the union which have prevail in the late election in surmount in favor of my humble pretension the difficulty which so often produce division in like occurrence it be obvious that other powerful cause indicate the great strength and stability of we union have essentially contribute to draw you together that these powerful cause exist and that they be permanent be my fixed opinion that they may produce a like accord in all question touch however remotely the liberty prosperity and happiness of we country will always be the object of my most fervent prayer to the supreme author of all good in a government which be found by the people who possess exclusively the sovereignty it seem proper that the person who may be place by they suffrage in this high trust should declare on commence its duty the principle on which he intend to conduct the administration if the person thus elect have serve the precede term a opportunity be afford he to review its principal occurrence and to give such further explanation respect they as in he judgment may be useful to he constituent the event of one year have influence on those of another and in like manner of a precede on the succeed administration the movement of a great nation be connect in all they part if error have be commit they ought to be correct if the policy be sound it ought to be support it be by a thorough knowledge of the whole subject that we fellow-citizen be enable to judge correctly of the past and to give a proper direction to the future just before the commencement of the last term the united state have conclude a war with a very powerful nation on condition equal and honorable to both party the event of that war be too recent and too deeply impressed on the memory of all to require a development from I we commerce have be in a great measure drive from the sea we atlantic and inland frontier be invade in almost every part the waste of life along we coast and on some part of we inland frontier to the defense of which we gallant and patriotic citizen be call be immense in addition to which not less than $ 120000000 be add at its end to the public debt as soon as the war have terminate the nation admonish by its event resolve to place itself in a situation which should be better calculate to prevent the recurrence of a like evil and in case it should recur to mitigate its calamity with this view after reduce we land force to the basis of a peace establishment which have be further modify since provision be make for the construction of fortification at proper point through the whole extent of we coast and such a augmentation of we naval force as should be well adapt to both purpose the law make this provision be pass in 1815 and 1816 and it have be since the constant effort of the executive to carry they into effect the advantage of these fortification and of a augmented naval force in the extent contemplate in a point of economy have be fully illustrate by a report of the board of engineer and naval commissioner lately communicate to congress by which it appear that in a invasion by 20000 man with a correspondent naval force in a campaign of six month only the whole expense of the construction of the work would be defray by the difference in the sum necessary to maintain the force which would be adequate to we defense with the aid of those work and that which would be incur without they the reason of this difference be obvious if fortification be judiciously place on we great inlet as distant from we city as circumstance will permit they will form the only point of attack and the enemy will be detain there by a small regular force a sufficient time to enable we militia to collect and repair to that on which the attack be make a force adequate to the enemy collect at that single point with suitable preparation for such other as might be menace be all that would be requisite but if there be no fortification then the enemy might go where he please and change he position and sailing from place to place we force must be call out and spread in vast number along the whole coast and on both side of every bay and river as high up in each as it might be navigable for ship of war by these fortification support by we navy to which they would afford like support we should present to other power a armed front from st croix to the sabine which would protect in the event of war we whole coast and interior from invasion and even in the war of other power in which we be neutral they would be find eminently useful as by keep they public ship at a distance from we city peace and order in they would be preserve and the government be protect from insult it need scarcely be remark that these measure have not be resort to in a spirit of hostility to other power such a disposition do not exist toward any power peace and good will have be and will hereafter be cultivate with all and by the most faithful regard to justice they have be dictate by a love of peace of economy and a earnest desire to save the life of we fellow-citizen from that destruction and we country from that devastation which be inseparable from war when it find we unprepared for it it be believe and experience have show that such a preparation be the best expedient that can be resort to to prevent war i add with much pleasure that considerable progress have already be make in these measure of defense and that they will be complete in a few year consider the great extent and importance of the object if the plan be zealously and steadily persevere in the conduct of the government in what relate to foreign power be always a object of the highest importance to the nation its agriculture commerce manufacture fishery revenue in short its peace may all be affect by it attention be therefore due to this subject at the period advert to the power of europe after have be engage in long and destructive war with each other have conclude a peace which happily still exist we peace with the power with whom we have be engage have also be conclude the war between spain and the colony in south america which have commence many year before be then the only conflict that remain unsettled this be a contest between different part of the same community in which other power have not interfere be not affect by they accommodation this contest be consider at a early stage by my predecessor a civil war in which the party be entitle to equal rights in we port this decision the first make by any power be form on great consideration of the comparative strength and resource of the party the length of time and successful opposition make by the colony and of all other circumstance on which it ought to depend be in strict accord with the law of nation congress have invariably act on this principle have make no change in we relation with either party we attitude have therefore be that of neutrality between they which have be maintain by the government with the strictest impartiality no aid have be afford to either nor have any privilege be enjoy by the one which have not be equally open to the other party and every exertion have be make in its power to enforce the execution of the law prohibit illegal equipment with equal rigor against both by this equality between the party they public vessel have be receive in we port on the same footing they have enjoy a equal right to purchase and export arm munitions of war and every other supply the exportation of all article whatever be permit under law which be pass long before the commencement of the contest we citizen have trade equally with both and they commerce with each have be alike protect by the government respect the attitude which it may be proper for the united state to maintain hereafter between the party i have no hesitation in state it as my opinion that the neutrality heretofore observe should still be adhere to from the change in the government of spain and the negotiation now depend invite by the corte and accept by the colony it may be presume that they difference will be settle on the term propose by the colony should the war be continue the united state regard its occurrence will always have it in they power to adopt such measure respect it as they honor and interest may require shortly after the general peace a band of adventurer take advantage of the law to its censure it belong to the executive not to suffer the execution under these decision to transcend the great purpose for which punishment be necessary the full benefit of example be government have declare its independence and that there be now no opposition to it there nor a force to make any for the last three year the government of spain have not send a single corps of troops to any part of that country nor be there any reason to believe it will send any in future thus it be manifest that all those province be not only in the full enjoyment of they independence but consider the state of the war and other circumstance that there be not the most remote prospect of they be deprive of it when the result of such a contest be manifestly settle the new government have a claim to recognition by other power which ought not to be resist civil war too often excite feeling which the party can not control the opinion entertain by other power as to the result may assuage those feeling and promote a accommodation between they useful and honorable to both the delay which have be observe in make a decision on this important subject will it be presume have afford a unequivocal proof to spain as it must have do to other power of the high respect entertain by the united state for she rights and of they determination not to interfere with they the province belong to this hemisphere be we neighbor and have successively as each portion of the country acquire its independence press they recognition by a appeal to fact not to be contest and which they think give they a just title to it to motive of interest this government have invariably disclaim all pretension be resolve to take no part in the controversy or other measure in regard to it which should not merit the sanction of the civilized world to other claim a just sensibility have be always feel and frankly acknowledge but they in themselves could never become a adequate cause of action it be incumbent on this government to look to every important fact and circumstance on which a sound opinion could be form which have be do when we regard then the great length of time which this war have be prosecute the complete success which have attend it in favor of the province the present condition of the party and the utter inability of spain to produce any change in it we be compel to conclude that its fate be settle and that the province which have declare they independence and be in the enjoyment of it ought to be recognize of the view of the spanish government on this subject no particular information have be recently receive it may be presume that the successful progress of the revolution through such a long series of year gain strength and extend annually in every direction and embrace by the late important event with little exception all the dominion of spain south of the united state on this continent place thereby the complete sovereignty over the whole in the hand of the people will reconcile the parent country to a accommodation with they on the basis of they unqualified independence nor have any authentic information be recently receive of the disposition of other power respect it a sincere desire have be cherish to act in concert with they in the propose recognition of which several be some time past duly apprise but it be understand that they be not prepare for it the immense space between those power even those which border on the atlantic and these province make the movement a affair of less interest and excitement to they than to we it be probable therefore that they have be less attentive to its progress than we have be it may be presume however that the late event will dispel all doubt of the result in propose this measure it be not contemplate to change thereby in the slightest manner we friendly relation with either of the party but to observe in all respects as heretofore should the war be continue the most perfect neutrality between they of this friendly disposition a assurance will be give to the government of spain to whom it be presume it will be as it ought to be satisfactory the measure be propose under a thorough conviction that it be in strict accord with the law of nation that it be just and right as to the party and that the united state owe it to they station and character in the world as well as to they essential interest to adopt it should congress concur in the view herein present they will doubtless see the propriety of make the necessary appropriation for carry it into effect jame monroe and provide for the defense of the coast immediately after the war be found on the marked event of that interesting epoch the vast body of man which it be find necessary to call into the field through the whole extent of we maritime frontier and the number who perish by exposure with the immense expenditure of money and waste of property which follow be to be trace in a eminent degree to the defenseless condition of the coast it be to mitigate these evil in future war and even for the higher purpose of prevent war itself that the decision be form to make the coast so far as it might be practicable impregnable and that the measure necessary to that great object have be pursue with so much zeal since it be know that no part of we union be more expose to invasion by the numerous avenue lead to it or more defenseless by the thinness of the neighbor population or offer a greater temptation to invasion either as a permanent acquisition or as a prize to the cupidity of grasp invader from the immense amount of produce deposit there than the city of new orlean it be know also that the seizure of no part of we union could affect so deeply and vitally the immediate interest of so many state and of so many of we fellow-citizen comprise all that extensive territory and numerous population which be connect with and dependent on the mississippus as the seizure of that city strong work well post be therefore deem absolutely necessary for its protection it be not however by the mississippus only or the water which communicate directly with or approach nearest to new orlean that the town be assailable it will be recollect that in the late war the public solicitude be excite not so much by the danger which menace it in those direction as by the apprehension that while a feint each instance consist in this that by the former he be to cause the arrangement to be make of the officer noncommissioned officer musician and private of the several _ corps of troops _ then in the service of the united state whereas in the latter the term _ troops _ be omit it can not be doubt that that omission have a object and that it be thereby intend to guard against misconstruction in so very material and important a circumstance by authorize the application of the act unequivocally to every corps of the staff as well as of the line with that word a much wider range be give to the act of 1815 on the reduction which then take place than under the last act the omission of it from the last act together with all the sanction which be give by congress to the construction of the law in the reduction make under the former could not fail to dispel all doubt as to the extent of the power grant by the last law and of the principle which ought to guide and on which it be thereby make the a officer may be reduce and arrange from one corps to another by a entire change of grade require a new commission and a new nomination to the senate i see no reason why a officer may not be advance staff of the army it be not perceive on what ground he appointment can be object to if such a construction be to be give to the act of 1821 as to confine the transfer of officer from the old to the new establishment to the _ corps of troops _ -- that be to the line of the army -- the whole staff of the army in every branch would not only be exclude from any appointment in the new establishment and they arrangement in it other consequence not less serious would follow if the right of the president to fill these original vacancy by the selection of officer from any branch of the whole military establishment be deny he would be compel to place in they officer of the same grade whose corps have be reduce and they with they the effect therefore of the law as to those appointment would be to legislate into office man who have be already legislate out of office take from the president all agency in they appointment such a construction would not only be subversive of the obvious principle of the constitution but utterly inconsistent with the spirit of the law itself since it would provide office for a particular grade and fix every member of that grade in those office at a of regiment of artillery a service in which they might have have no experience and for which they might in consequence be unqualified have omit in the message to congress at the commencement of the authorize the removal of one officer from a particular station and the location of another in it reduce the latter from a higher to a inferior grade with the advice and consent of the senate it surely justify under the latter law the arrangement of these officer with a like sanction to office of new creation from which no one have be remove and to which no one have a just claim it be on the
