object to its passage and to return the bill to the house of representative in which it originate under a conviction that congress do not possess the power under the constitution to pass such a law a power to establish turnpike with gate and toll and to enforce the collection of toll by penalty imply a power to adopt and execute a complete system of internal improvement a right to impose duty to be pay by all person pass a certain road and on horse and carriage as be do by this bill involve the right to take the land from the proprietor on a valuation and to pass law for the protection of the road from injury and if it exist as to one road it exist as to any other and to as many road as congress may think proper to establish a right to legislate for one of these purpose be a right to legislate for the other it be a complete right of jurisdiction and sovereignty for all the purpose of internal improvement and not merely the right of apply money under the power vest in congress to make appropriation under which power with the consent of the state through which this road pass the work be originally commence and have be so far execute i be of opinion that congress do not possess this power that the state individually can not grant it for although they may assent to the appropriation of money within they limit for such purpose they can grant no power of jurisdiction or sovereignty by special compact with the united state this power can be grant only by a amendment to the constitution and in the mode prescribe by it if the power exist it must be either because it have be specifically grant to the united state or that it be incidental to some power which have be specifically grant if we examine the specific grant of power we do not find it among they nor be it incidental to any power which have be specifically grant it have never be contend that the power be specifically grant it be claim only as be incidental to some one or more of the power which be specifically grant the follow be the power from which it be say to be derive : first from the right to establish post-office and post-road second from the right to declare war third to regulate commerce fourth to pay the debt and provide for the common defense and general welfare fifth from the power to make all law necessary and proper for carry into execution all the power vest by the constitution in the government of the united state or in any department or officer thereof sixth and lastly from the power to dispose of and make all needful rule and regulation respect the territory and other property of the united state accord to my judgment it can not be derive from either of those power nor from all of they unite and in consequence it do not exist have state my objection to the bill i should now cheerfully communicate at large the reason on which they be found if i have time to reduce they to such form as to include they in this paper the advanced stage of the session render that impossible have at the commencement of my service in this high trust consider it a duty to express the opinion that the united state do not possess the power in question and to suggest for the consideration of congress the propriety of recommend to the state a amendment to the constitution to vest the power in the united state my attention have be often draw to the subject since in consequence whereof i have occasionally commit my sentiment to paper respect it the form which this exposition have assume be not such as i should have give it have it be intend for congress nor be it conclude nevertheless as it contain my view on this subject be one which i deem of very high importance and which in many of its bearing have now become peculiarly urgent i will communicate it to congress if in my power in the course of the day or certainly on Monday next jame monroe washington _ may 4 1822 _ _ to the house of representative _ : i transmit the paper allude to in the message of this day on the subject of internal improvement jame monroe view of the president of the united state on the subject of internal improvement it may be presume that the proposition relate to internal improvement by road and canal which have be several time before congress will be take into consideration again either for the purpose of recommend to the state the adoption of a amendment to the constitution to vest the necessary power in the general government or to carry the system into effect on the principle that the power have already be grant it seem to be the prevailing opinion that great advantage would be derive from the exercise of such a power by congress respect the right there be much diversity of sentiment it be of the highest importance that this question should be settle if the right exist it ought forthwith to be exercise if it do not exist surely those who be friend to the power ought to unite in recommend a amendment to the constitution to obtain it i propose to examine this question the inquiry confine to its proper object and within the most limited scale be extensive we government be unlike other government both in its origin and form in analyze it the difference in certain respects between it and those of other nation ancient and modern necessarily come into view i propose to notice these difference so far as they be connect with the object of inquiry and the consequence likely to result from they vary in equal degree from those which have attend other government the digression if it may be so call will in every instance be short and the transition to the main object immediate and direct to do justice to the subject it will be necessary to mount to the source of power in these state and to pursue this power in its gradation and distribution among the several department in which it be now vest the great division be between the state government and the general government if there be a perfect accord in every instance as to the precise extent of the power grant to the general government we should then know with equal certainty what be the power which remain to the state government since it would follow that those which be not grant to the one would remain to the other but it be on this point and particularly respect the construction of these power and they incident that a difference of opinion exist and hence it be necessary to trace distinctly the origin of each government the purpose intend by it and the means adopt to accomplish they by have the interior of both government fully before we we shall have all the means which can be afford to enable we to form a correct opinion of the endowment of each before the revolution the present state then colony be separate community unconnected with each other except in they common relation to the crown they government be institute by grant from the crown which operate accord to the condition of each grant in the nature of a compact between the settler in each colony and the crown all power not retain in the crown be vest exclusively in the colony each have a government consist of a executive a judiciary and a legislative assembly one branch of which be in every instance elect by the people no office be hereditary nor do any title under the crown give rank or office in any of the colony in resist the encroachment of the parent country and abrogate the power of the crown the authority which have be hold by it vested exclusively in the people of the colony by they be a congress appoint compose of delegate from each colony who manage the war declare independence treat with foreign power and act in all thing accord to the sense of they constituent the declaration of independence confirm in form what have before exist in substance it announce to the world new state possess and exercise complete sovereignty which they be resolve to maintain they be soon after recognize by france and other power and finally by great britain herself in 1783 soon after the power of the crown be annul the people of each colony establish a constitution or frame of government for themselves in which these separate branch -- legislative executive and judiciary -- be institute each independent of the other to these branch each have its appropriate portion the whole power of the people not delegate to congress be communicate to be exercise for they advantage on the representative principle by person of they appointment or otherwise derive they authority immediately from they and hold they office for state term all the power necessary for useful purpose hold by any of the strongest government of the old world not vest in congress be impart to these state government without other check than such as be necessary to prevent abuse in the form of fundamental declaration or bill of right the great difference between we government and those of the old world consist in this that the former be representative the person who exercise they power do it not for themselves or in they own right but for the people and therefore while they be in the highest degree efficient they can never become oppressive it be this transfer of the power of the people to representative and responsible body in every branch which constitute the great improvement in the science of government and form the boast of we system it combine all the advantage of every known government without any of they disadvantage it retain the sovereignty in the people while it avoid the tumult and disorder incident to the exercise of that power by the people themselves it possess all the energy and efficiency of the most despotic government while it avoid all the oppression and abuse inseparable from those government in every stage of the conflict from its commencement until march 1781 the power of congress be undefined but of vast extent the assembly or convention of the several colony be form by representative from every county in each colony and the congress by delegate from each colonial assembly the power of the latter for general purpose resemble those of the former for local they rest on the same basis the people and be complete for all the purpose contemplate never be a movement so spontaneous so patriotic so efficient the nation exert its whole faculty in support of its rights and of its independence after the contest take that direction and it succeed it be however foresee at a very early stage that although the patriotism of the country might be rely on in the struggle for its independence a well-digested compact would be necessary to preserve it after obtain a plan of confederation be in consequence propose and take into consideration by congress even at the moment when the other great act which sever they from great britain and declare they independence be proclaim to the world this compact be ratify on the 21st march 1781 by the last state and thereupon carry into immediate effect the follow power be vest in the united state by the article of confederation as this the first bond of union be in operation nearly eight year during which time a practical construction be give to many of its power all of which be adopt in the constitution with important addition it be think that a correct view of those power and of the manner in which they be execute may shed light on the subject under consideration it may fairly be presume that where certain power be transfer from one instrument to the other and in the same term or term descriptive only of the same power that it be intend that they should be construe in the same sense in the latter that they be in the former article i declare that the style of the confederacy shall be the united state of america article ii each state retain its sovereignty freedom and independence and every power and right which be not expressly delegate to the united state article iii the state severally enter into a firm league of friendship with each other for they common defense the security of they liberty and they mutual and general welfare binding themselves to assist each other against all force offer to or attack make upon they on account of religion sovereignty trade etc article iv the free inhabitant of each state pauper vagabond and fugitive from justice excepted shall be entitle to all the privilege and immunity of free citizen in the several state etc fugitive from justice into any of the state shall be deliver up on the demand of the executive of the state from which they flee full faith and credit shall be give in each state to the record and act of every other state article v delegate shall be annually appoint by the legislature of each state to meet in congress on the first Monday in November with a power to recall etc no state shall appoint less than two nor more than seven nor shall any delegate hold he office for more than three in six year each state shall maintain its own delegate each state shall have one vote freedom of speech shall not be impeach and the member shall be protect from arrest except for treason etc article vi no state shall send or receive a embassy or enter into a treaty with a foreign power nor shall any person hold any office of profit or trust under the united state or any state accept any present emolument office or title from a foreign power nor shall the united state or any state grant any title of nobility no two state shall enter into any treaty without the consent of congress no state shall lay any impost or duty which may interfere with any treaty enter into by the united state no state shall engage in war unless it be invade or menace with invasion by some indian tribe nor grant letter of marque or reprisal unless it be against pirate nor keep up vessel of war nor any body of troops in time of peace without the consent of congress but every state shall keep up a well regulate militia etc article vii when land force be raise by any state for the common defense all officer of and under the rank of colonel shall be appoint by the legislature of each state article viii all charge of war and all other expense which shall be incur for the common defense or general welfare shall be defray out of a common treasury which shall be supply by the several state in proportion to the value of all the land in each state grant to individual the tax for pay each proportion shall be levy by the several state article ix congress shall have the sole and exclusive right and power of determine on peace and war except in the case mention in the sixth article of send and receive ambassador enter into alliance except etc of establish rule for decide what capture on land and water shall be legal of grant letter of marque and reprisal in time of peace appoint court for the trial of piracy and felony on the high sea for decide controversy between the state and between individual claim land under two or more state whose jurisdiction have be adjust of regulate the alloy and value of coin strike by they authority and of foreign coin fix the standard of weight and measure regulate the trade with the indian establish and regulate post office from one state to another and throughout all the state and exact such postage as may be requisite to defray the expense of the office of appoint all officer of the land force except the regimental appoint all the officer of the naval force to ascertain the necessary sum of money to be raise for the service of the united state and appropriate the same to borrow money and emit bill of credit to build and equip a navy to agree on the number of land force and to make requisition on each state for its quota that the assent of nine state shall be requisite to these great act article x regulate the power of the committee of the state to sit in the recess of congress article xi provide for the admission of canada into the confederation article xii pledge the faith of the united state for the payment of all bill of credit issue and money advantage which would be derive from such improvement be incalculable the facility which would thereby be afford to the transportation of the whole of the rich production of we country to market would alone more than amply compensate for all the labor and expense attend they great however as be that advantage it be one only of many and by no mean the most important every power of the general government and of the state government connect with the strength and resource of the country would be make more efficient for the purpose intend by they in war they would facilitate the transportation of man ordnance and provision and munitions of war of every kind to every part of we extensive coast and interior on which a attack might be make or threaten those who have any knowledge of the occurrence of the late war must know the good effect which would result in the event of another war from the command of a interior navigation alone along the coast for all the purpose of war as well as of commerce between the different part of we union the impediment to all military operation which proceed from the want of such a navigation and the reliance which be place notwithstanding those impediment on such a commerce can not be forget in every other line they good effect would be most sensibly feel intelligence by means of the post-office department would be more easily extensively and rapidly diffuse part the most remote from each other would be bring more closely together distant land would be make more valuable and the industry of we fellow-citizen on every portion of we soil be better reward it be natural in so great a variety of climate that there should be a corresponding difference in the produce of the soil that one part should raise what the other might want it be equally natural that the pursuit of industry should vary in like manner that labor should be cheaper and manufacture succeed better in one part than in another that be the climate the most severe and the soil less productive navigation the fishery and commerce should be most rely on hence the motive for a exchange for mutual accommodation and active intercourse between they each part would thus find for the surplus of its labor in whatever article it consist a extensive market at home which would be the most profitable because free from duty there be another view in which these improvement be of still more vital importance the effect which they would have on the bond of union itself afford a inducement for they more powerful than any which have be urge or than all of they unite the only danger to which we system be expose arise from its expansion over a vast territory we union be not hold together by stand army or by any tie other than the positive interest and powerful attraction of its part toward each other ambitious man may hereafter grow up among we who may promise to themselves advancement from a change and by practice upon the sectional interest feeling and prejudice endeavor under various pretext to promote it the history of the world be replete with example of this kind -- of military commander and demagogue become usurper and tyrant and of they fellow-citizen become they instrument and slave i have little fear of this danger know well how strong the bond which hold we together be and who the people be who be thus hold together but still it be proper to look at and to provide against it and it be not within the compass of human wisdom to make a more effectual provision than would be make by the propose improvement with they aid and the intercourse which would grow out of they the part would soon become so compacted and bind together that nothing could break it the expansion of we union over a vast territory can not operate unfavorably to the state individually on the contrary it be believe that the greater the expansion within practicable limit -- and it be not easy to say what be not so -- the greater the advantage which the state individually will derive from it with government separate vigorous and efficient for all local purpose they distance from each other can have no injurious effect upon they respective interest it have already be show that in some important circumstance especially with the aid of these improvement they must derive great advantage from that cause alone -- that be from they distance from each other in every other way the expansion of we system must operate favorably for every state in proportion as it operate favorably for the union it be in that sense only that it can become a question with the state or rather with the people who compose they as state they can be affect by it only by they relation to each other through the general government and by its effect on the operation of that government manifest it be that to any extent to which the general government can sustain and execute its function with complete effect will the state -- that be the people who compose they -- be benefit it be only when the expansion shall be carry beyond the faculty of the general government so as to enfeeble its operation to the injury of the whole that any of the part can be injure the tendency in that stage will be to dismemberment and not to consolidation this danger should therefore be look at with profound attention as one of a very serious character i will remark here that as the operation of the national government be of a general nature the state have complete power for internal and local purpose the expansion may be carry to very great extent and with perfect safety it must be obvious to all that the further the expansion be carry provide it be not beyond the just limit the greater will be the freedom of action to both government and the more perfect they security and in all other respects the better the effect will be to the whole american people extent of territory whether it be great or small give to a nation many of its characteristic it mark the extent of its resource of its population of its physical force it mark in short the difference between a great and a small power to what extent it may be proper to expand we system of government be a question which do not press for a decision at this time at the end of the revolutionary war in 1783 we have as we contend and believe a right to the free navigation of the mississippus but it be not until state sustain the strength and energy of they character acquire the province of louisiana with the free navigation of the river from its source to the ocean and a liberal boundary on the western side other consideration than those which have dictate the course heretofore pursue at whatever point we may stop whether it be at a single range of state beyond the mississippus or by take a greater scope the advantage of such improvement be deem of the highest importance it be so on the present scale the further we go the greater will be the necessity for they it can not be doubt that improvement for great national purpose would be better make by the national government than by the government of the several state we experience prior to the adoption of the constitution demonstrate that in the exercise by the individual state of most of the power grant to the united state a contract rivalry of interest and misapply jealousy of each other have a important influence on all they measure to the government proceed from these and other cause to act as a nation and to perform all the duty which the nation owe to itself under any system which leave the general government dependent on the state which produce the transfer of these power to the united state by the establishment of the present constitution the reasoning which be applicable to the grant of any of the power now vest in congress be likewise so at least to a certain extent to that in question it be natural that the state individually in make improvement should look to they particular and local interest the member compose they respective legislature represent the people of each state only and might not feel themselves at liberty to look to object in these respects beyond that limit if the resource of the union be to be disadvantage of the system as well as discredit to both government but congress would look to the whole and make improvement to promote the welfare of the whole it be the peculiar felicity of the propose amendment that while it will enable the united state to accomplish every national object the improvement make with that view will eminently promote the welfare of the individual state who may also add such other as they own particular interest may require the situation of the cumberland road require the particular and early attention of congress be form over very lofty mountain and in many instance over deep and wide stream across which valuable bridge have be erect which be sustain by stone wall as be many other part of the road all these work be subject to decay have decay and will decay rapidly unless timely and effectual measure be adopt to prevent it the declivity from the mountain and all the height must suffer from the frequent and heavy fall of water and its descent to the valley as also from the deep congelation during we severe winter other injury have also be experience on this road such as the displace the cap of the wall and other work commit by worthless people either from a desire to render the road impassable or to have the transportation in another direction or from a spirit of wantonness to create employment for idler these consideration show that a active and strict police ought to be establish over the whole road with power to make repair when necessary to establish turnpike and toll as the means of raise money to make they and to prosecute and punish those who commit waste and other injury should the united state be willing to abandon this road to the state through which it pass would they take charge of it each of that portion within its limit and keep it in repair it be not to be presume that they would since the advantage attend it be exclusively national by connect as it do the atlantic with the western state and in a line with the seat of the national government the most expensive part of this road lie within pennsylvanium and virginium very near the confines of each state and in a route not essentially connect with the commerce of either if it be think proper to vest this power in the united state the only mode in which it can be do be by a amendment of the constitution the state individually can not transfer the power to the united state nor can the united state receive it the constitution form a equal and the sole relation between the general government and the several state and it recognize no change in it which shall not in like manner apply to all if it be once admit that the general government may form compact with individual state not common to the other and which the other might even disapprove into what pernicious consequence might it not lead such compact be utterly repugnant to the principle of the constitution and of the most dangerous tendency the state through which this road pass have effect on all the great interest of we union it be however my opinion that the power should be confine to great national work only since if it be unlimited it would be liable to abuse and might be productive of evil for all minor improvement the resource of the state individually would be fully adequate and by the state such improvement might be make with greater advantage than by the union as they would understand better such as they more immediate and local interest require in the view above present i have think it proper to trace the origin of we institution and particularly of the state useful knowledge will keep it within a just subordination and at the same time elevate it to the highest purpose this object seem to be essentially obtain in this institution and with great advantage to the union the military academy form the basis in regard to science on which the military establishment rest it furnish annually after due examination and on the report of the academic staff many to those of the post-office department can not be estimate too highly this great work be likewise a ornament and a honor to the nation believe that a competent power to adopt and execute a system of it advisable that a amendment of the constitution to that effect should be recommend to the several state a bill which assume the right to adopt and execute such a system have be present for my signature at the last session i be compel from the view which i have take of the power of the general government to negative it on which occasion i think it proper to communicate the sentiment which i have form on mature consideration on the whole subject to that communication in all the view in which the great interest to which it relate may be suppose to merit you attention i have now to refer should congress however deem it improper to recommend such a amendment they have accord to my judgment the right to keep the road in repair by provide for the superintendence of it and appropriate the money necessary for repair surely if they have the right to appropriate money to make the road they have a right to appropriate it to preserve the road from ruin from the exercise of this power no danger be to be apprehend under we happy system the people be the sole and exclusive fountain of power each government originate from they and to they alone each to its proper constituent be they respectively and solely responsible for the faithful discharge of they duty within they constitutional limit and that the people will confine they public agent of every station to the strict line of they constitutional duty there be no cause to doubt have however communicate my sentiment to congress at the last session fully in the document to which i have refer respect the right of appropriation as distinct from the right of jurisdiction and sovereignty over the territory in question i deem it improper to enlarge on the subject here from the best information that i have be able to obtain it appear that we manufacture though depressed immediately after the peace have considerably increase and be still increase under the encouragement give they by the tariff of 1816 and by subsequent law satisfied i be whatever may be the abstract doctrine in favor of unrestricted commerce provide all nation would concur in it and it be not liable to be interrupt by war which have never occur and can not be expect that there be other strong reason applicable to we situation and relation with other country which impose on we the obligation to cherish and sustain we manufacture satisfied however i likewise be that the interest of every part of we union even of those most benefit by manufacture require that this subject should be touch with the greatest caution and a critical knowledge of the united state would have have equal weight with other power and that spain herself yield to those magnanimous feeling of which she history furnish so many example would have terminate on that basis a controversy so unavailing and at the same time so destructive we still cherish the hope that this result will not long be postpone sustain we neutral position and allow to each party while the war continue equal rights it be incumbent on the united state to claim of each with equal rigor the faithful observance of we rights accord to the well-known law of nation from each therefore a like enthusiastic zeal and devotion in favor of public and personal liberty be associate with we recollection of ancient greece that such a country should have be overwhelm and so long hide as it be from the world under a gloomy despotism have be a cause of unceasing and deep regret to generous mind for age past it be natural therefore that the reappearance of those people in they original character contend in favor of they liberty should produce that great excitement and sympathy in they favor which have be so signally display throughout the united state a strong hope be entertain that these people will recover they independence and resume they equal station among the nation of the earth a great effort have be make in spain and portugal to improve the condition of the people and it must be very console to all benevolent mind to see the extraordinary moderation with which it have be conduct that it may promote the happiness of both nation be the ardent wish of this whole people to the expression of which we confine ourselves for whatever may be the feeling or sentiment which every individual under we government have a right to indulge and express it be nevertheless a sacred maxim equally with the government and people that the destiny of every independent nation in what relate to such improvement of right belong and ought to be leave exclusively to themselves whether we reason from the late war or from those menacing symptom which now appear in europe it be manifest that if a convulsion should take place in any of those country it will proceed from cause which have no existence and be utterly unknown in these state in which there be but one order that of the people to whom the sovereignty exclusively belong should war break out in any of those country who can foretell the extent to which it may be carry or the desolation which it may spread exempt as we be from these cause we internal tranquillity be secure and distant as we be from the troubled scene and faithful to first principle in regard to other power we might reasonably presume that we should not be molest by they this however ought not to be calculate on as certain unprovoked injury be often inflict and even the peculiar felicity of we situation might with some be a cause for excitement and aggression the history of the late war in europe furnish a complete demonstration that no system of conduct however correct in principle can protect neutral power from injury from any party that a defenseless position and distinguish love of peace be the surest invitation to war and that there be no way to avoid it other than by be always prepared and willing for just cause to meet it if there be a people on earth whose more especial duty it be to be at all time prepare to defend the rights with which they be bless and to surpass all other in sustain the necessary burden and in submit to sacrifice to make such preparation it be undoubtedly the people of these state when we see that a civil war of the most frightful character rage from the adriatic to the black sea that strong symptom of war appear in other part proceed from cause which should it break out may become general and be of long duration that the war still continue between spain and the independent government she late province in this hemisphere that it be likewise menace between portugal and brazil in consequence of the attempt of the latter to dismember itself from the former and that a system of piracy of great extent be maintain in the neighbor sea which will require equal vigilance and decision to suppress it the reason for sustain the attitude which we now hold and for push forward all we measure of defense with the utmost vigor appear to I to acquire new force the united state owe to the world a great example and by means thereof to the cause of liberty and humanity a generous support they have so far succeed to the satisfaction of the virtuous and enlighten of every country there be no reason to doubt that they whole movement will be regulate by a sacred regard to principle all we institution be found on that basis the ability to support we own cause under any trial to which it may be expose be the great point on which the public solicitude rest it have be often charge against free government that they have neither the foresight nor the virtue to provide at the proper season for great emergency that they course be improvident and expensive that war will always find they unprepared and whatever may be its calamity that its terrible warning will be disregard and forget as soon as that a great effort be then make in spain and portugal to improve the condition of the people of those country and that it appear to be conduct with extraordinary moderation it need scarcely be remark always be anxious and interested spectator the citizen of the united state cherish sentiment the most friendly in favor of the liberty and happiness of they fellow-men on that side of the atlantic in the war of the european power in matter relate to themselves we have never take any part nor do it comport with we policy so to do it be only when we rights be invade or seriously menace that we resent injury or make preparation for we defense with the movement in this hemisphere we be of necessity more immediately connect and by cause which must be obvious to all enlighten and impartial observer the political system of the ally power be essentially different in this respect from that of america this difference proceed from that which exist in they respective government and to the defense of we own which have be achieve by the loss of so much blood and treasure and mature by the wisdom of they most enlighten citizen and under which we have enjoy unexampled felicity this whole nation be devote we owe it therefore to candor and to the amicable relation exist between the united state and those power to declare that we should consider any attempt on they part to extend they system to any portion of this hemisphere as dangerous to we peace and safety with the exist colony or dependency of any european power we have not interfere and shall not interfere but with the government who have declare they independence and maintain it and whose independence we have on great consideration and on just principle acknowledge we could not view any interposition for the purpose of oppress they or control in any other manner they destiny by any european power in any other light than as the manifestation of a unfriendly disposition toward the united state in the war between those new government and spain we declare we neutrality at the time of they recognition and to this we have adhere and shall continue to adhere provide no change shall occur which in the judgment of the competent authority of this government shall make a corresponding change on the part of the united state indispensable to they security the late event in spain and portugal shew that europe be still unsettled of this important fact no stronger proof can be adduce than that the ally power should have think it proper on any principle satisfactory to themselves to have interpose by force in the internal concern of spain to what extent such interposition may be carry on the same principle be a question in which all independent power whose government differ from theirs be interested even those most remote and surely none more so than the united state we policy in regard to europe which be adopt at a early stage of the war which have so long agitate that quarter of the globe nevertheless remain the same which be not to interfere in the internal concern of any of its power to consider the government _ de facto _ as the legitimate government for we to cultivate friendly relation with it and to preserve those relation by a frank firm and manly policy meeting in all instance the just claim of every power submit to injury from none but in regard to those continent circumstance be eminently and conspicuously different it be impossible that the ally power should extend they political system to any portion of either continent without endanger we peace and happiness nor can anyone believe that we southern brethren if leave to themselves would adopt it of they own accord it be equally impossible therefore that we should behold such interposition in any form with indifference if we look to the comparative strength and resource of spain and those new government and they distance from each other it must be obvious that she can never subdue they it be still the true policy of the united state to leave the party to themselves in the hope that other power will pursue the same course if we compare the present condition of we union with its actual state at the close of we revolution the history of the world furnish no example of a progress in improvement in all the important circumstance which constitute the happiness of a nation which bear any resemblance to it at the first epoch we population do not exceed 3000000 by the last census it amount to about 10000000 and what be more extraordinary it be almost altogether native for the immigration from other country have be inconsiderable at the first epoch half the territory within we acknowledged limit be uninhabited and a wilderness since then new territory have be acquire of vast extent comprise within it many river particularly the mississippus the navigation of which to the ocean be of the highest importance to the original state over this territory we population have expand in every direction and new state have be establish almost equal in number to those which form the first bond of we union this expansion of we population and accession of new state to we union have have the happiest effect on all its highest interest that it have eminently augmented we resource and add to we strength and respectability as a power be admit by all but it be not in these important circumstance only that this happy effect be feel it be manifest that by enlarge the basis of we system and increase the number of state the system itself have be greatly strengthen in both its branch consolidation and disunion have thereby be render equally impracticable each government confide in its own strength have less to apprehend from the other and in consequence each enjoy a greater freedom of action be render more efficient for all the purpose for which it be institute it be unnecessary to treat here of the vast improvement make in the system itself by the adoption of this constitution and of its happy effect in elevate the character and in protect the rights of the nation as well as of individual to what then do we owe these blessing it be know to all that we derive they from the excellence of we institution ought we not then to adopt every measure which may be necessary to perpetuate they jame monroe special message washington city _ December 7 1823 _ _ 1824 _ _ to the house of representative of the united state _ : in compliance with a resolution of the house of representative of the 15th of December last request the president of the united state to communicate a plan for a peace establishment of the navy of the united state i herewith transmit a report from the secretary of the navy which contain the plan require in present this plan to the consideration of congress i avail myself of the occasion to make some remark on it which the importance of the subject require and experience justify if a system of universal and permanent peace could be establish or if in war the belligerent party would respect the rights of neutral power we should have no occasion for a navy or a army the expense and danger of such establishment might be avoid the history of all age prove that this can not be presume on the contrary that at least one-half of every century in ancient as well as modern time have be consume in war and often of the most general and desolating character nor be there any cause to infer if we examine the condition of the nation with which we have the most intercourse and strongest political relation that we shall in future be exempt from that calamity within any period to which a rational calculation may be extend and as to the rights of neutral power it be sufficient to appeal to we own experience to demonstrate how little regard will be pay to they whenever they come in conflict with the interest of the power at war while we rely on the justice of we cause and on argument alone the amount of the property of we fellow-citizen which be seize and confiscate or destroy by the belligerent party in the war of the french revolution and of those which follow before we become a party to the war be almost incalculable the whole movement of we government from the establishment of we independence have be guide by a sacred regard for peace situate as we be in the new hemisphere distant from europe and unconnected with its affair bless with the happiest government on earth and have no object of ambition to gratify the united state have steadily cultivate the relation of amity with every power and if in any european war a respect for we rights might be rely on it be undoubtedly in those to which i have advert the conflict be vital the force be nearly equally balanced and the result uncertain each party have the strongest motive of interest to cultivate we good will lest we might be throw into the opposite scale powerful as this consideration usually be it be nevertheless utterly disregard in almost every stage of and by every party to those war to these encroachment and injury we regard for peace be finally force to yield in the war to which at length we become a party we whole coast from st croix to the mississippus be either invade or menace with invasion and in many part with a strong impose force both land and naval in those part where the population be most dense the pressure be comparatively light but there be scarcely a harbor or city on any of we great inlet which could be consider secure new york and philadelphium be eminently expose the then exist work not be sufficient for they protection the same remark be applicable in a certain extent to the city eastward of the former and as to the condition of the whole country southward of the latter the event which mark the war be too recent to require detail we army and navy signalize themselves in every quarter where they have occasion to meet they gallant foe and the militia voluntarily fly to they aid with a patriotism and fight with a bravery which exalt the reputation of they government and country and which do they the highest honor in whatever direction the enemy choose to move with they squadron and to land they troops we fortification where any exist present but little obstacle to they they pass those work without difficulty they squadron in fact annoy we whole coast not of the sea only but every bay and great river throughout its whole extent in enter those inlet and sail up they with a small force the effect be disastrous since it never fail to draw out the whole population on each side and to keep it in the field while the squadron remain there the expense attend this species of defense with the exposure of the inhabitant and the waste of property may readily be conceive the occurrence which precede the war and those which attend it be alike replete with useful instruction as to we future policy those which mark the first epoch demonstrate clearly that in the war of other power we can rely only on force for the protection of we neutral rights those of the second demonstrate with equal certainty that in any war in which we may be engage hereafter with a strong naval power the expense waste and other calamity attend it consider the vast extent of we maritime frontier can not fail unless it be defend by adequate fortification and a suitable naval force to correspond with those which be experience in the late war two great object be therefore to be regard in the establishment of a adequate naval force : the first to prevent war so far as it may be practicable the second to diminish its calamity when it may be inevitable hence the subject of defense become intimately connect in all its part in war and in peace for the land and at sea no government will be dispose in its war with other power to violate we rights if it know we have the means be prepared and resolve to defend they the motive will also be diminish if it know that we defens by land be so well plan and execute that a invasion of we coast can not be productive of the evil to which we have heretofore be expose it be under a thorough conviction of these truth derive from the admonition of the late war that congress as early as the year 1816 during the term of my enlighten and virtuous predecessor under whom the war have be declare prosecute and terminate digest and make provision for the defense of we country and support of its rights in peace as well as in war by act which authorize and enjoin the augmentation of we navy to a prescribe limit and the construction of suitable fortification throughout the whole extent of we maritime frontier and wherever else they might be deem necessary it be to the execution of these work both land and naval and under a thorough conviction that by hasten they completion i should render the best service to my country and give the most effectual support to we free republican system of government that my humble faculty would admit of that i have devote so much of my time and labor to this great system of national policy since i come into this office and shall continue to do it until my retirement from it at the end of you next session the navy be the arm from which we government will always derive most aid in support of we neutral rights every power engage in war will know the strength of we naval force the number of we ship of each class they condition and the promptitude with which we may bring they into service and will pay due consideration to that argument justice will always have great weight in the cabinet of europe but in long and destructive war exigency often occur which press so vitally on they that unless the argument of force be bring to its aid it will be disregard we land force will always perform they duty in the event of war but they must perform it on the land we navy be the arm which must be principally rely on for the annoyance of the commerce of the enemy and for the protection of we own and also by cooperation with the land force for the defense of the country capable of move in any and every direction it possess the faculty even when remote from we coast of extend its aid to every interest on which the security and welfare of we union depend annoy the commerce of the enemy and menacing in turn its coast provide the force on each side be nearly equally balanced it will draw its squadron from we own and in case of invasion by a powerful adversary by a land and naval force which be always to be anticipate and ought to be provide against we navy may by like cooperation with we land force render essential aid in protect we interior from incursion and depredation the great object in the event of war be to stop the enemy at the coast if this be do we city and whole interior will be secure for the accomplishment of this object we fortification must be principally rely on by place strong work near the mouth of we great inlet in such position as to command the entrance into they as may be do in many instance it will be difficult if not impossible for ship to pass they especially if other precaution and particularly that of steam battery be resort to in they aid in the war between other power into which we may be draw in support of we neutral rights it can not be doubt that this defense would be adequate to the purpose intend by it nor can it be doubt that the knowledge that such work exist would form a strong motive with any power not to invade we rights and thereby contribute essentially to prevent war there be it be admit some entrance into we interior which be of such vast extent that it would be utterly impossible for any work however extensive or well post to command they of this class the chesapeake bay which be a arm of the sea may be give as a example but in my judgment even this bay may be defend against any power with whom we may be involve in war as a third party in the defense of we neutral rights by erect strong work at the mouth of jame river on both side near the cape as we be now do and at old point comfort and the rip rap and connect those work together by chain whenever the enemy 's force appear place in the rear some large ship and steam battery the passage up the river would be render impracticable this guard would also tend to protect the whole country border on the bay and river empty into it as the hazard would be too great for the enemy however strong he naval force to ascend the bay and leave such a naval force behind since in the event of a storm whereby he vessel might be separate or of a calm the ship and steam battery behind the work might rush forth and destroy they it could only be in the event of a invasion by a great power or a combination of several power and by land as well as by naval force that those work could be carry and even then they could not fail to retard the movement of the enemy into the country and to give time for the collection of we regular troops militia and volunteer to that point and thereby contribute essentially to he ultimate defeat and expulsion from we territory under a strong impression that a peace establishment of we navy be connect with the possible event of war and that the naval force intend for either state however small it may be be connect with the general system of public defense i have think it proper in communicate this report to submit these remark on the whole subject jame monroe washington _ February 2 1824 _ _ to the house of representative of the united state _ : in compliance with a resolution _ _ to the senate and house of representative of the united state _ : i herewith transmit to congress certain document relate to a claim of massachusett for service render by the militia of that state in the late war and for which payment be make by the state from the particular circumstance attend this claim i have think it proper to submit the subject to the consideration of congress in form a just estimate of this claim it will be necessary to recur to the cause which prevent its admission or the admission of any part thereof at a earlier day it will be recollect that when a call be make on the militia of that state for service in the late war under a arrangement which be alike applicable to the militia of all the state and in conformity with the act of congress the executive of massachusett refuse to comply with the call on the principle that the power vest in congress by the constitution to provide for call forth the militia to execute the law of the union suppress insurrection and repel invasion be not a complete power for those purpose but conditional and dependent on the consent of the executive of the several state and also that when call into service such consent be give they could not be command by a regular officer of the united state or other officer than of the militia except by the president in person that this decision of the executive of massachusett be repugnant to the constitution of the united state and of dangerous tendency especially when it be consider that we be then engage in a war with a powerful nation for the defense of we common rights be the decide opinion of this government and when the period at which that decision be form be consider it be as early as the 5th of August 1812 immediately after the war be declare and that it be not relinquish during the war it be infer by the executive of the united state that the decision of the executive of that state be alike applicable to all the service that be render by the militia of the state during the war in the correspondence with the governor of massachusett at that important epoch and on that very interesting subject it be announce to he by the secretary of war that if the militia of the state be call into service by the executive of the state and not put under the command of the major-general of the united state as the militia of the other state be the expense attend they service would be chargeable to the state and not to the united state it be also state to he at the same time that any claim which the state might have for the reimbursement of such expense could not be allow by the executive of the united state since it would involve principle on which that branch of the government could not decide under these circumstance a decision on the claim of the state of massachusett have hitherto be suspend and it need not be remark that the suspension have proceed from a conviction that it would be improper to give any sanction by its admission or by the admission of any part thereof either to the construction of the constitution contend for by the then executive of that state or to its conduct at that period toward the general government and the union in January 1823 the representative in congress from massachusett and maine suggest by memorial that the constitutional objection could not apply to a portion of the claim and request that the accounting officer of the government might be instruct to audit and admit such part as might be free from that objection in all case where claim be present for militia service it be the duty and the practice of the accounting officer to submit they to the department for instruction as to the legality of the claim that be whether the service have be render by order of the competent authority or otherwise under circumstance to justify the claim against the united state admit that the evidence in support of it should be satisfactory to this request there appear to be no well-founded objection under the reservation as to the constitutional principle and accordingly a order be give to the accounting officer of the treasury to proceed in auditing the claim with that reservation in conformity with this arrangement the executive of massachusett appoint two citizen of that state commissioner to attend to the settlement of its claim and who in execution of the trust repose in they have present to the accounting officer of the treasury that portion comprehend the service of the fifth division of the militia of the state which have be audit and report for consideration subject to the objection above state i have examine this report with the document present by the commissioner and be of opinion that the service render by that division be spontaneous patriotic and proper necessary for self-defense to repel in some instance actual invasion and in other to meet by adequate preparation invasion that be menace the commissioner of the state have intimate that other portion of service stand on similar ground the accounting officer have be instruct in auditing the whole to do it in such manner as to enable the department to show distinctly under what circumstance each portion of service be render whether voluntary call out by invasion or the menace of invasion or by public authority and in such case whether the militia render such service be place under the authority of the united state or retain under that of the state it afford I great pleasure to state that the present executive of massachusett have disclaim the principle which be maintain by the former executive and that in this disclaimer both branch of the legislature have concur by this renunciation the state be place on the same ground in this respect with the other state and this very distressing anomaly in we system be remove it be well know that the great body of we fellow-citizen in massachusett be as firmly devote to we union and to the free republican principle of we government as we fellow-citizen of the other state of this important truth they conduct in every stage of we revolutionary struggle and in many other emergency bear ample testimony and i add with profound interest and a thorough conviction that although the difficulty advert to in the late war with they executive excited equal surprise and regret it be not believe to extend to they there never be a moment when the confidence of the government in the great body of we fellow-citizen of that state be impaired nor be a doubt entertain that they be at all time willing and ready to support they rights and repel a invasion by the enemy the commissioner of massachusett have urge in compliance with they instruction the payment of so much of they claim as apply to the service render by the fifth division which have be audit and i should have no hesitation in admit it if i do not think under all the circumstance of the case that the claim in all its part be cognizable by congress alone the period at which the constitutional difficulty be raise by the executive of the state be in the highest degree important as be the tendency of the principle for which it contend and which be adhere to during the war the public mind throughout the union be much excite by that occurrence and great solicitude be feel as to its consequence the executive of the united state be bind to maintain and do maintain a just construction of the constitution in do which it be gratify to recollect that the most friendly feeling be cherish toward they brethren of that state the executive of the state be warn in the correspondence which then take place of the light in which its conduct be view and of the effect it would have so far as related to the right of the executive of the united state on any claim which might afterwards be present by the state to compensation for such service under these circumstance the power of the executive of the united state to settle any portion of this claim seem to be preclude it seem proper also that this claim should be decide on full investigation before the public that the principle on which it be decide may be thoroughly understand by we fellow-citizen of every state which can be do by congress alone who alone also possess the power to pass law which may be necessary to carry such decision into effect in submit this subject to the calm and enlighten judgment of congress i do it with peculiar satisfaction from a knowledge that you be now place by the course of event in a situation which will enable you to adopt such measure as will not only comport with the sound principle of we government but likewise be conducive to other the highest interest of we union by the renunciation of the principle maintain by the then executive of massachusett as have be do by its present executive and both branch of the legislature in the most formal manner and in accord with the sentiment of the great body of the people the constitution be restore in a very important feature -lrb- that connect with the public defense -rrb- and in the most important branch -lrb- that of the militia -rrb- to its native strength it be very gratifying to know that this renunciation have be produce by the regular orderly and pacific operation of we republican system whereby those who be in the right at the moment of difficulty and who sustain the government with great firmness have daily gain strength until this result be accomplish the point on which you will have to decide be what be fairly due for the service which be actually render by what mean shall we contribute most to cement the union and give the greatest support to we most excellent constitution in seek each object separately we be lead to the same result all that can be claim by we fellow-citizen of massachusett be that the constitutional objection be waive and that they be place on the same footing with they brethren in the other state that regard the service render by the militia of other state for which compensation have be make give to the rule the most liberal construction like compensation be make for similar service render by the militia of that state i have be lead to conclude on great consideration that the principle of justice as well as a due regard for the great interest of we union require that this claim in the extent propose should be accede to essential service be render in the late war by the militia of massachusett and with the most patriotic motive it seem just therefore that they should be compensate for such service in like manner with the militia of the other state the constitutional difficulty do not originate with they and have now be remove it comport with we system to look to the service render and to the intention with which it be render and to award the compensation accordingly especially as it may now be do without the sacrifice of principle the motive in this instance be the stronger because well satisfied i be that by so do we shall give the most effectual support to we republican institution no latent cause of discontent will be leave behind the great body of the people will be gratify and even those who now survive who be then in error can not fail to see with interest and satisfaction this distressing occurrence thus happily terminate i therefore consider it my duty to recommend it to congress to make provision for the settlement of the claim of massachusett for service render in the late war by the militia of the state in conformity with the rule which have govern in the settlement of the stipulation be a full proof i have also be animated since i come into this office with the same zeal from a anxious desire to meet the wish of the state and in the hope that by the establishment of these tribe beyond the mississippus they improvement in civilization they security and happiness would be promote by the paper bearing date on the 30th of January last which be communicate to the chief of the cherokee nation in this city who come to protest against any further appropriation of money for hold treaty with they the obligation impose on the united state by the compact with georgium to extinguish the indian title to the right of soil within the state and the incompatibility with we system of they existence as a distinct community within any state be press with the utmost earnestness it be propose to they at the same time to procure and convey to they territory beyond the mississippus in exchange for that which they hold within the limit of georgium or to pay they for it its value in money to this proposal they answer which bear date 11th of February follow give a unqualified refusal by this it be manifest that at the present time and in they present temper they can be remove only by force to which should it be deem proper the power of the executive be incompetent i have no hesitation however to declare it as my opinion that the indian title be not affect in the slightest circumstance by the compact with georgium and that there be no obligation on the united state to remove the indian by force the express stipulation of the compact that they title should be extinguish at the expense of the united state when it may be do _ peaceably _ and on _ reasonable _ condition be a full proof that it be the clear and distinct understanding of both party to it that the indian have a right to the territory in the disposal of which they be to be regard as free agent a attempt to remove they by force would in my opinion be unjust in the future measure to be adopt in regard to the indian within we limit and in consequence within the limit of any state the united state have duty to perform and a character to sustain to which they ought not to be indifferent at a early period they improvement in the art of civilized life be make a object with the government and that have since be persevere in this policy be dictate by motive of humanity to the aborigine of the country and under a firm conviction that the right to adopt and pursue it be equally applicable to all the tribe within we limit my impression be equally strong that it would promote essentially the security and happiness of the tribe within we limit if they could be prevail on to retire west and north of we state and territory on land to be procure for they by the united state in exchange for those on which they now reside surround as they be and press as they will be on every side by the white population it will be difficult if not impossible for they with they kind of government to sustain order among they they interior will be expose to frequent disturbance to remedy which the interposition of the united state will be indispensable and thus they government will gradually lose its authority until it be annihilate in this process the moral character of the tribe will also be lose since the change will be too rapid to admit they improvement in civilization to enable they to institute and sustain a government found on we principle if such a change be compatible either with the compact with georgium or with we general system or to become member of a state should any state be willing to adopt they in such number regard the good order peace and tranquillity of such state but all these evil may be avoid if these tribe will consent to remove beyond the limit of we present state and territory land equally good and perhaps more fertile may be procure for they in those quarter the relation between the united state and such indian would still be the same consideration of humanity and benevolence which have now great weight would operate in that event with a augmented force since we should feel sensibly the obligation impose on we by the accommodation which they thereby afford we place at ease as the united state would then be the improvement of those tribe in civilization and in all the art and usage of civilized life would become the part of a general system which might be adopt on great consideration and in which every portion of we union would then take a equal interest these view have steadily be pursue by the executive and the money which have be place at its disposal have be so apply in the manner best calculate accord to its judgment to produce this desirable result as will appear by the document which accompany the the state which ought to be execute in all its condition with perfect good faith in do this however it be the duty of the united state to regard its strict import and to make no sacrifice of they interest not call for by the compact nor contemplated by either of the party when it be enter into nor to commit any breach of right or of humanity in regard to the indian repugnant to the judgment and revolt to the feeling of the whole american people i submit the subject to you consideration in full confidence that you will duly weigh the obligation of the compact with georgium its import in of that act i refer to its fourth and fifth section which be in the follow word : sec 4 _ and be it further enact _ that if any citizen of the united state be of the crew or ship 's company of any foreign ship or vessel engage in the slave trade or any person whatever be of the crew or ship 's company of any ship or vessel own in the whole or part or navigate for or in behalf of any citizen or several maritime power of europe and america as he may deem expedient for the effectual abolition of the african slave trade and its ultimate denunciation as piracy under the law of nation by the consent of the civilized world by the act of congress above refer to whereby the most effectual means that could be devise be adopt for the extirpation of the slave trade the wish of the united state be explicitly declare that all nation might concur in a similar policy it could only be by such concurrence that the great object could be accomplish and it be by negotiation and treaty alone that such concurrence could be obtain commence with one power and extend it to other the course therefore which the executive who have concur in the act have to pursue be distinctly mark out for it have there however be any doubt respect it the resolution of the house of representative the branch which might with strict propriety express its opinion could not fail to have remove it by the tenth article of the treaty of peace between the united state and great britain conclude at ghent it be stipulate that both party should use they best endeavor to accomplish the abolition of the african slave trade this object have be accordingly pursue by both government with great earnestness by separate act of legislation and by negotiation almost uninterrupted with the purpose of establish a conceit between they in some measure which might secure its accomplishment great britain in she negotiation with other power have conclude treaty with spain portugal and the netherland in which without constitute the crime as piracy or class it with crime of that denomination the party have concede to the naval officer of each other the right of search and capture of the vessel of either that might be engage in the slave trade and have institute court consist of judge subject of both party for the trial of the vessel so capture in the negotiation with the united state great britain have earnestly and repeatedly press on they the adoption of similar provision they have be resist by the executive on two grounds : one that the constitution of mixed tribunal be incompatible with they constitution and the other that the concession of the right of search in time of peace for a offense not piratical would be repugnant to the feeling of the nation and of dangerous tendency the right of search be the right of war of the belligerent toward the neutral to extend it in time of peace to any object whatever might establish a precedent which might lead to other with some power and which even if confine to the instance specify might be subject to great abuse animated by a ardent desire to suppress this trade the united state take stronger ground by make it by the act above refer to piratical a measure more adequate to the end and free from many of the objection applicable to the plan which have be propose to they it be this alternative which the executive under the sanction and injunction above state offer to the british government and which that government have accept by make the crime piracy the right of search attach to the crime and which when adopt by all nation will be common to all and that it will be so adopt may fairly be presume if steadily persevere in by the party to the present convention in the meantime and with a view to a fair experiment the obvious course seem to be to carry into effect with every power such treaty as may be make with each in succession in present this alternative to the british government it be make a indispensable condition that the trade should be make piratical by act of parliament as it have be by a act of congress this be provide for in the convention and have since be comply with in this respect therefore the nation rest on the same ground suitable provision have also be adopt to protect each party from the abuse of the power grant to the public ship of the other instead of subject the person detect in the slave trade to trial by the court of the captor as would be the case if such trade be piracy by the law of nation it be stipulate that until that event they shall be try by the court of they own country only hence there could be no motive for a abuse of the right of search since such abuse could not fail to terminate to the injury of the captor should this convention be adopt there be every reason to believe that it will be the commencement of a system destine to accomplish the entire abolition of the slave trade great britain by make it she own confessedly adopt at the suggestion of the united state and be pledge to propose and urge its adoption by other nation in concert with the united state will find it for she interest to abandon the less-effective system of she previous treaty with spain portugal and the netherland and to urge on those and other power they accession to this the crime will then be universally proscribe as piracy and the traffic be suppress forever other consideration of high importance urge the adoption of this convention we have at this moment pend with great britain sundry other negotiation intimately connect with the welfare and even the peace of we union in one of they nearly a third part of the territory of the state of maine be in contestation in another the navigation of the st lawrence the admission of consul into the british island and a system of commercial intercourse between the united state and all the british possession in this hemisphere be subject of discussion in a third we territorial and other rights upon the northwest coast be to be adjust while a negotiation on the same interest be open with russium in a fourth all the most important controvertible point of maritime law in time of war be bring under consideration and in the fifth the whole system of south american concern connect with a general recognition of south american independence may again from hour to hour become as it have already be a object of concerted operation of the highest interest to both nation and to the peace of the world it can not be disguise that the rejection of this convention can not fail to have a very injurious influence on the good understanding between the two government on all these point that it would place the executive administration under embarrassment and subject it the congress and the nation to the charge of insincerity respect the great result of the final suppression of the slave trade and that its first and indispensable consequence will be to constrain the executive to suspend all further negotiation with every european and american power to which overture have be make in compliance with the resolution of the house of representative of 28th February 1823 must be obvious to invite all nation with the statute of piracy in we hand to adopt its principle as the law of nation and yet to deny to all the common right of search for the pirate whom it would be impossible to detect without enter and search the vessel would expose we not simply to the charge of inconsistency it must be obvious that the restriction of search for pirate to the african coast be incompatible with the idea of such a crime it be not doubt also if the convention be adopt that no example of the commission of that crime by the citizen or subject of either power will ever occur again it be believe therefore that this right as applicable to piracy would not only extirpate the trade but prove altogether innocent in its operation in further illustration of the view of congress on this subject i transmit to the senate extract of we affair foreign and domestic realize the most sanguine anticipation which have be entertain of the public prosperity if we look to the whole we growth as a nation continue to be rapid beyond with fraternal affection experience have already shewn that the difference of climate and of industry proceeding from that cause inseparable from such vast domain and which under other system might have a repulsive tendency can not fail to produce with we under wise regulation the opposite effect what one portion want the other may supply and this will be most sensibly feel by the part most distant from each other form thereby a domestic market and a active intercourse between the extreme and throughout every portion of we union thus by a happy distribution of power between the national and state government government which rest exclusively on the sovereignty of the people and be fully adequate to the great purpose for which they be respectively institute cause which might otherwise lead to dismemberment operate powerfully to draw we closer together in every other circumstance a correct view of the actual state of we union must be equally gratifying to we constituent we relation necessarily be attend with expense and that not inconsiderable but it be doubt whether any other can be devise which would be less liable to that objection or more likely to succeed in look to the interest which the united state have on the pacific ocean and on the western coast of this continent the propriety of establish a military post at the mouth of columbium river or at some other point
