mountain would be essentially promote to carry this object into effect the appropriation of a adequate sum to authorize the employment of a frigate with a officer of the corps of engineer to explore the mouth of the columbium river and the coast contiguous thereto to enable the executive to make such establishment at the most suitable point be recommend to congress it be think that attention be purpose from the view above present it be manifest that the situation of the united state be in the highest degree prosperous and happy there be no object which as a people we can desire which we do not possess or which be not within we reach bless with government the happiest which the world ever know with no distinct order in society or divide interest in any portion of the vast territory over which they dominion extend we have every motive to cling together which can animate a virtuous and enlighten people the great object be to preserve these blessing and to hand they down to the latest danger we should pay the most vigilant and unceasing attention remove the cause where it may be practicable and be prepare to meet it when inevitable against foreign danger the policy of the government seem to be already settle the event of the late war admonish we to make we maritime frontier impregnable by a well-digested chain of fortification and to give efficient protection to we commerce by augment we navy to a certain extent which have be steadily pursue and which it be incumbent upon we to complete as soon as circumstance will permit in the event of war it be on the maritime frontier that we shall be assail it be in that quarter therefore that we should be prepare to meet the attack it be there that we whole force will be call into action to prevent the destruction of we town and the desolation and pillage of the interior to give full effect to this policy great improvement will be indispensable access to those work by every practicable communication should be make easy and in every direction the intercourse between every part of we union should also be promote and facilitate by the exercise of those power which may comport with a faithful regard washington _ January 27 1825 _ _ to the senate and house of representative of the united state _ : be deeply impressed with the opinion that the removal of the indian tribe from the land which they now occupy within the limit of the several state and territory to the country lie westward and northward thereof within we acknowledged boundary be of very high importance to we union and may be accomplish on condition and in a manner to promote the interest and happiness of those tribe the attention of the government have be long draw with great solicitude to the object for the removal of the tribe within the limit of the state of georgium the motive have be peculiarly strong arise from the compact with that state whereby the united state be bind to extinguish the indian title to the land within it whenever it may be do peaceably and on reasonable condition in the fulfillment of this compact i have think that the united state should act with a generous spirit that they should omit nothing which should comport with a liberal construction of the instrument and likewise be in accordance with the just rights of those tribe from the view which i have take of the subject i be satisfied that in the discharge of these important duty in regard to both the party allude to the united state will have to encounter no conflicting interest with either on the contrary that the removal of the tribe from the territory which they now inhabit to that which be designate in the message at the commencement of the session which would accomplish the object for georgium under a well-digested plan for they government and civilization which should be agreeable to themselves would not only shield they from impend ruin but promote they welfare and happiness experience have clearly demonstrate that in they present state it be impossible to incorporate they in such mass in any form whatever into we system it have also demonstrate with equal certainty that without a timely anticipation of and provision against the danger to which they be expose under cause which it will be difficult if not impossible to control they degradation and extermination will be inevitable the great object to be accomplish be the removal of these tribe to the territory designate on condition which shall be satisfactory to themselves and honorable to the united state this can be do only by convey to each tribe a good title to a adequate portion of land to which it may consent to remove and by provide for it there a system of internal government which shall protect they property from invasion and by the regular progress of improvement and civilization prevent that degeneracy which have generally mark the transition from the one to the other state i transmit herewith a report from the secretary of war which present the best estimate which can be form from the document in that department of the number of indian within we state and territory and of the amount of land hold by the several tribe within each of the state of the country lie northward and westward thereof within we acknowledged boundary of the part to which the indian title have already be extinguish and of the condition on which other part in a amount which may be adequate to the object contemplate may be obtain by this report it appear that the indian title have already be extinguish to extensive tract in that quarter and that other portion maybe acquire to the extent desire on very moderate condition satisfied i also be that the removal propose be not only practicable but that the advantage attend it to the indian may be make so apparent to they that all the tribe even those most oppose may be induce to accede to it at no very distant day the digest of such a government with the consent of the indian which should be endow with sufficient power to meet all the object contemplate -- to connect the several tribe together in a bond of amity and preserve order in each to prevent intrusion on they property to teach they by regular instruction the art of civilized life and make they a civilized people -- be a object of very high importance it be the powerful consideration which we have to offer to these tribe as a inducement to relinquish the land on which they now reside and to remove to those which be designate it be not doubt that this arrangement will present consideration of sufficient force to surmount all they prejudice in favor of the soil of they nativity however strong they may be they elder have sufficient intelligence to discern the certain progress of event in the present train and sufficient virtue by yield to momentary sacrifice to protect they family and posterity from inevitable destruction they will also perceive that they may thus attain a elevation to which as community they could not otherwise aspire to the united state the propose arrangement offer many important advantage in addition to those which have be already enumerate by the establishment of such a government over these tribe with they consent we become in reality they benefactor the relation of conflict interest which have heretofore exist between they and we frontier settlement will cease there will be no more war between they and the united state adopt such a government they movement will be in harmony with we and its good effect be feel throughout the whole extent of we territory to the pacific it may fairly be presume that through the agency of such a government the condition of all the tribe inhabit that vast region may be essentially improve that permanent peace may be preserve with they and we commerce be much extend with a view to this important object i recommend it to congress to adopt by solemn declaration certain fundamental principle in accord with those above suggest as the basis of such arrangement as may be enter into with the several tribe to the strict observance of which the faith of the nation shall be pledge i recommend it also to congress to provide by law for the appointment of a suitable number of commissioner who shall under the direction of the president be authorize to visit and explain to the several tribe the object of the government and to make with they accord to they instruction such arrangement as shall be best calculate to carry those object into effect a negotiation be now depend with the creek nation for the cession of land hold by it within the limit of georgium and with a reasonable prospect of success it be presume however that the result will not be know during the present session of congress to give effect to this negotiation and to the negotiation which it be propose to hold with all the other tribe within the limit of the several state and territory on the principle and for the purpose state it be recommend that a adequate appropriation be now make by congress jame monroe washington _ January 27 1825 _ _ to the senate of the united state _ : i transmit to the senate a treaty conclude in this ratification jame monroe washington _ February 21 1825 _ the president of the senate pro tempore : i transmit to the senate a convention of general peace amity navigation and commerce sign by the plenipotentiary of the united state and of the republic of colombium at bogota on the 3d of October 1824 together with the document appertain to the negotiation of the same for the constitutional consideration of the senate with regard to its ratification jame monroe washington _ February 23 1825 _ _ to the house of representative _ : i transmit to the house of representative a further report from the secretary of state in pursuance of they resolution of the 1st instant with the papers to which it refer upon the subject of the capture and detention of american fisherman the past season in the bay of fundy jame monroe washington _ February 25 1825 _ _ to the senate and house of representative _ : i communicate herewith to both house of congress copy of the treaty between the united state and the quapaw nation of indian conclude at harrington in the territory of arkansa on the 15th day of November last and between the united state and the choctaw nation of indian conclude at the city of washington on the 20th day of January last which have be duly ratify jame monroe washington _ February 26 1825 _ _ to the senate and house of representative of the united state _ : just before the termination of the last session a act entitle a act concern wreck on the coast of florida which then pass be present to I with many other and approve and as i think sign a report to that effect be then make to congress it appear however after the adjournment that the evidence of such approbation have not be attach to it whether the act may be consider in force under such circumstance be a point on which it belong not to I to decide to remove all doubt on the subject i submit to the consideration of congress the propriety of pass a declaratory act to that effect jame monroe washington _ February 28 1825 _ _ to the senate of the united state _ : i transmit to the senate for the exercise of its constitutional power a treaty lately conclude at the indian spring by commissioner of the united state duly authorize with the chief of the creek nation assemble there in council with the document connect therewith jame monroe proclamation -lrb- from senate journal eighteenth congress second session p 269 -rrb- washington _ January 19 1825 _ _ the president of the united state to ------ senator for the state of ------ _ : certain matter touch the public good require that the senate of the united state should be convene on Friday the 4th day of march next you be desire to attend at the senate chamber in the city of washington on that day then and there to receive and deliberate on such communication as shall be make to you jame monroe end of the project gutenberg ebook of a compilation of the message and papers of the president by jame d richardson
